2:34:2372:0:14:72:525:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Debt Relief and Debtor Outcomes: Measuring the Effects of Consumer Bankruptcy Protection
2:35:2460:14:14:72:198:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Will Dobbie and Jae Song
2:36:2484:14:14:72:234:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:NBER Working Paper No. 20520
2:37:2512:14:14:72:150:658:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:September 2014
2:38:2526:14:28:72:155:644:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:JEL No. J22,K35
2:39:2541:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:40:2549:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Consumer bankruptcy is one of the largest social insurance programs in the United States, but little
2:41:2649:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:is known about its impact on debtors. We use 500,000 bankruptcy filings matched to administrative
2:42:2746:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:tax and foreclosure data to estimate the impact of Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection on subsequent
2:43:2843:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:outcomes. Exploiting the random assignment of bankruptcy filings to judges, we find that Chapter
2:44:2939:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:13 protection increases annual earnings by $5,562, decreases five-year mortality by 1.2 percentage
2:45:3037:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:points, and decreases five-year foreclosure rates by 19.1 percentage points. These results come primarily
2:46:3142:14:42:72:487:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:from the deterioration of outcomes among dismissed filers, not gains by granted filers.
2:47:3229:42:14:72:132:462:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Will Dobbie
2:48:3240:14:14:72:205:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Industrial Relations Section
2:49:3268:14:14:72:172:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Princeton University
2:50:3288:14:14:72:156:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Firestone Library
2:51:3305:14:14:72:198:406:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Princeton, NJ 08544-2098
2:52:3329:14:14:72:124:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:and NBER
2:53:3337:14:28:72:190:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:wdobbie@princeton.edu
2:54:3358:28:14:72:115:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Jae Song
2:55:3366:14:14:72:221:336:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Social Security Administration
2:56:3396:14:14:72:232:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Office of Disability Adjudication
2:57:3429:14:14:72:129:308:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:and Review
2:58:3439:14:14:72:226:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:5107 Leesburg Pike, Suite 1400
2:59:3469:14:14:72:190:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Falls Church, VA 22041
2:60:3491:14:0:72:158:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:jae.song@ssa.gov
3:61:3507:0:17:115:512:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:“The Bankruptcy Act is...of public as well as private interest, in that it gives to the
3:62:3594:17:16:99:512:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:honest but unfortunate debtor...a new opportunity in life and a clear field for future
3:63:3680:16:17:99:466:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effort, unhampered by the pressure and discouragement of pre-existing debt.”
3:64:3756:17:28:115:438:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:- U.S. Supreme Court,Local Loan Co.v.Hunt, 292 U.S. 234 (1934)
3:65:3818:28:17:88:539:631:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In 2010, 1.5 million Americans filed for over $450 billion in debt relief through the consumer
3:66:3912:17:16:72:540:614:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy system.1American households receive more resources through the bankruptcy system
3:67:4003:16:16:72:540:598:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:than through all state unemployment insurance programs combined (Lefgren, McIntyre, and Miller
3:68:4097:16:17:72:540:582:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2010), with nearly one in ten American households having filed for bankruptcy at some point
3:69:4188:17:16:72:540:565:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(Stavins 2000). The U.S. bankruptcy system is also among the most generous in the world, allowing
3:70:4285:16:17:72:540:549:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:debtors to choose between Chapter 7 bankruptcy that provides debt relief and protection from wage
3:71:4382:17:16:72:540:532:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:garnishment in exchange for a debtor’s non-exempt assets, and Chapter 13 bankruptcy that adds
3:72:4475:16:17:72:422:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the protection of most assets in exchange for a partial repayment of debt.
3:73:4549:17:16:88:539:499:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Despite providing billions of dollars in debt relief each year, it is not clear how bankruptcy pro-
3:74:4648:16:17:72:540:483:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tection impacts debtors. In theory, bankruptcy protection increases an individual’s incentive to work
3:75:4749:17:16:72:540:466:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and prevents any sharp drops in consumption that may have important long-term consequences,
3:76:4840:16:16:72:540:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:such as becoming sick due to the lack of medical care or losing one’s home through foreclosure.
3:77:4935:16:17:72:540:434:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Yet, in practice, households work about the same number of hours (Han and Li 2007), accumu-
3:78:5026:17:16:72:540:417:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:late less wealth (Han and Li 2011), and have less access to credit (Cohen-Cole, Duygan-Bump and
3:79:5121:16:17:72:540:401:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Montoriol-Garriga 2009) after receiving bankruptcy protection, leading some to conclude that the
3:80:5217:17:16:72:540:384:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:benefits of debt relief have been overstated (Porter and Thorne 2006). The lack of demonstrable
3:81:5312:16:17:72:540:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:benefits, combined with a rapid increase in the number of bankruptcy filings, led Congress to enact
3:82:5411:17:16:72:524:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:new barriers to filing in the 2005 Bankruptcy Abuse Prevention and Consumer Protection Act.
3:83:5502:16:16:88:539:335:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Empirically estimating the impact of bankruptcy protection has been complicated by two impor-
3:84:5595:16:17:72:540:319:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tant issues. First, there is little information on the long-term outcomes of most bankruptcy filers.
3:85:5695:17:16:72:540:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Bankruptcy filers are not tracked in a systematic way after filing and datasets such as the PSID
3:86:5791:16:17:72:540:286:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and NLSY include only a few hundred bankrupt households. Second, most comparisons are biased
3:87:5883:17:16:72:540:269:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:due to selection and endogeneity problems. Bankruptcy filers are likely to have had worse outcomes
3:88:5981:16:17:72:540:253:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:even before filing, biasing cross-sectional comparisons (e.g. Han and Li 2007, 2011), and most prox-
3:89:6081:17:16:72:540:236:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:imate causes of bankruptcy such as job loss and health shocks also impact later outcomes, biasing
3:90:6178:16:16:72:540:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:within-individual comparisons (e.g. Cohen-Cole, Duygan-Bump and Montoriol-Garriga 2009). The
3:91:6270:16:17:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:lack of an unbiased counterfactual control group may help explain why the previous literature has
3:92:6367:17:16:72:383:187:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:found little evidence that bankruptcy protection benefits debtors.
3:93:6433:16:17:88:539:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In this paper, we use a new dataset linking 500,000 bankruptcy filings to administrative tax
3:94:6525:17:16:72:540:154:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:records from the Social Security Administration (SSA) and administrative foreclosure records to
3:95:6620:16:17:72:540:138:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimate the causal effect of Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection on subsequent earnings, mortality,
3:96:6717:17:24:72:540:121:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and home foreclosure. Our empirical strategy exploits the fact that most U.S. bankruptcy courts use
3:97:6816:24:15:87:379:97:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:1Non-business Chapter 7 and Chapter 13 filing statistics are available at
3:98:6889:15:10:72:462:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:http://www.uscourts.gov/uscourts/Statistics/BankruptcyStatistics/BAPCPA/2010/Table1A.pdf
3:99:6977:10:0:72:463:72:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:http://www.uscourts.gov/uscourts/Statistics/BankruptcyStatistics/BAPCPA/2010/Table1D.pdf
4:100:7066:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a blind rotation system to assign cases to judges, effectively randomizing filers to judges within each
4:101:7169:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:office. Moreover, while there are uniform criteria by which a judge may dismiss a bankruptcy filing,
4:102:7269:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:there is significant variation in the interpretation of these criteria across judges (Sullivan, Warren,
4:103:7372:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Westbrook 1994, Norberg and Compo 2007, Chang and Schoar 2008).  As a result, other-
4:104:7460:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:wise identical filers are assigned to judges with substantially different rates of granting bankruptcy
4:105:7562:17:16:72:123:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection.
4:106:7573:16:17:88:539:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Using these differences in judge leniency as an instrumental variable for bankruptcy protection,
4:107:7669:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we are able to identify the ex-post impact of Chapter 13 on the marginal recipient of protection –
4:108:7767:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers whose bankruptcy decision is altered by the judge assignment due to disagreement on whether
4:109:7865:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:or not they should receive bankruptcy protection. The identified parameter holds fixed any ex-
4:110:7959:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ante impacts of bankruptcy, such as over-borrowing, moral hazard in the workplace (White 2011),
4:111:8054:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:entrepreneurial risk-taking (Fan and White 2003, Armour and Cumming 2008), or the crowding out
4:112:8148:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of formal insurance (Mahoney 2012). Our empirical strategy is similar to Kling (2006), which uses
4:113:8245:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the random assignment of judges to estimate the ex-post impact of sentence length on earnings, and
4:114:8343:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:subsequent research that estimates the ex-post effects of foster care (Doyle 2007, 2008), juvenile
4:115:8441:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:incarceration (Aizer and Doyle 2013), corporate bankruptcy (Chang and Schoar 2008), temporary-
4:116:8535:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:help employment (Autor and Houseman 2010), and Disability Insurance (French and Song 2011,
4:117:8625:17:16:72:242:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Maestas, Mullen, and Strand 2013).
4:118:8659:16:17:88:539:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In our empirical analysis, we find compelling evidence that Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection
4:119:8751:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:benefits debtors. Over the first five post-filing years, Chapter 13 protection increases the marginal
4:120:8852:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:recipient’s annual earnings by $5,562, a 25.1 percent increase from the pre-filing mean. Employment
4:121:8951:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:increases by 6.8 percentage points over the same time period, an 8.3 percent increase. Five-year
4:122:9047:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mortality decreases by 1.2 percentage points, a 30.0 percent decrease from the dismissed filer mor-
4:123:9146:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tality rate, and five-year home foreclosure rates decrease by 19.1 percentage points, a more than
4:124:9243:17:16:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:100 percent decrease from the dismissed filer foreclosure rate. There is also evidence that Chapter
4:125:9342:16:17:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:13 protection deceases the receipt of Supplemental Security Income (SSI), although there is little
4:126:9440:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to no impact on 401k contributions and the receipt of Disability Insurance (DI). Descriptive results
4:127:9540:16:17:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:suggest that the estimated impacts come from the deterioration of outcomes among dismissed filers,
4:128:9638:17:16:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:not gains by granted filers. Filers granted bankruptcy protection have similar pre- and post-filing
4:129:9737:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:earnings. In contrast, dismissed filers experience large and persistent drops in earnings after filing
4:130:9839:17:16:72:145:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for bankruptcy.
4:131:9854:16:16:88:539:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We find evidence of two mechanisms through which bankruptcy protection benefits filers. First,
4:132:9948:16:17:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we find that the impact of Chapter 13 protection is larger when creditors are allowed to garnish a
4:133:10046:17:16:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:debtor’s earnings. Exploiting within- and across-state variation in the marginal garnishment rate,
4:134:10144:16:17:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we find that the implied earnings elasticity with respect to potential garnishment is 0.94. These
4:135:10241:17:16:72:540:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:results are consistent with the idea that bankruptcy protection maintains the incentive to work
4:136:10336:16:17:72:540:117:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by preventing an increase in the effective marginal tax rate on earnings. Second, we find results
4:137:10433:17:16:72:540:100:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:suggesting that Chapter 13 protection helps to maintain economic stability by reducing foreclosures
4:138:10532:16:0:72:540:84:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and by reducing strategic moves to evade creditors. The marginal recipient of Chapter 13 protection
5:139:10632:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is 24.6 percentage points more likely to work in his or her pre-filing job, 23.8 percentage points more
5:140:10735:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:likely to work in the same industry, and 15.3 percentage points more likely to work in the same
5:141:10830:16:17:72:98:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:state.
5:142:10836:17:16:88:539:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There are three important caveats to our analysis. First, our identification strategy measures the
5:143:10934:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effect of Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection for the marginal recipient. It is possible that the impact
5:144:11035:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Chapter 13 protection is different for filers who are not on the margin of receipt. To partially
5:145:11134:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:address this issue, we estimate marginal treatment effects (MTEs) that measure the change in
5:146:11226:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:outcomes for the marginal recipient of bankruptcy protection as we move from more strict judges to
5:147:11324:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:more lenient judges. The MTE results suggest that the effects of Chapter 13 protection are slightly
5:148:11423:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:larger for less deserving filers. Second, we are only able to use our instrumental variables strategy in
5:149:11527:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy offices that randomly assign filings to judges. While our instrumental variables sample
5:150:11625:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is broadly similar to the full sample of Chapter 13 filers, it is possible that the effect of bankruptcy
5:151:11729:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:may differ in the two samples. To provide some evidence on this issue, we estimate the impact
5:152:11822:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Chapter 13 in both samples using an event study methodology that does not rely on random
5:153:11913:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:assignment. We find that the impact of Chapter 13 protection is similar in our instrumental variables
5:154:12014:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and full samples, though the point estimates are somewhat smaller in our full sample. Third, we are
5:155:12113:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:unable to use our instrumental variables strategy to estimate the impact of Chapter 7 bankruptcy
5:156:12209:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection, which make up approximately 75 percent of all bankruptcy filings.  Using our event
5:157:12303:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:study design, we find that the effect of Chapter 7 protection is more modest than that of Chapter
5:158:12400:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:13 protection. Filers granted Chapter 7 bankruptcy protection earn $1,639 to $1,936 more than
5:159:12493:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:dismissed filers over the first five post-filing years and are 2.7 percentage points more likely to be
5:160:12595:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:employed over the same time period. Filers granted Chapter 7 also have five-year foreclosure rates
5:161:12693:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that are 1.7 percentage points lower than dismissed filers, but are neither more nor less likely to be
5:162:12795:16:17:72:326:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:deceased after five years compared to dismissed filers.
5:163:12850:17:16:88:539:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The remainder of the paper is structured as follows. Section I provides a brief overview of the
5:164:12945:16:17:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:consumer bankruptcy system in the United States. Section II describes our data and provides sum-
5:165:13041:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mary statistics. Section III presents a stylized model that motivates our empirical exercise. Section
5:166:13142:16:17:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:IV describes our empirical strategy.  Section V estimates the impact of Chapter 13 bankruptcy
5:167:13235:17:33:72:484:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection on labor supply, mortality, and home foreclosure, and Section VI concludes.
5:168:13321:33:21:197:415:215:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:I. Consumer Bankruptcy in the U.S.
5:169:13355:21:24:275:336:194:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A. Overview
5:170:13366:24:16:72:540:170:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Bankruptcy is the legal process to resolve unpaid debts. In the United States, individual debtors
5:171:13463:16:24:72:460:154:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f4:are allowed to choose between Chapter 7 and Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection.2
5:172:13541:24:15:87:539:130:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:2The most commonly reported cause of bankruptcy is an unexpected income or expense shock. In a hand-collected
5:173:13650:15:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:sample of bankruptcy filers, 67.5 percent of filers report job loss as a precipitating factor, 22.1 percent report family
5:174:13771:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:issues such as divorce, and 19.3 report medical expenses (Sullivan, Warren, and Westbrook 2000), with other work
5:175:13883:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:suggesting a somewhat larger role for medical expenses (Domowitz and Sartain 1999, Warren, Sullivan, and Jacoby
5:176:13994:11:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:2000, Himmelstein et al. 2009). Using similar data from PSID, Fay, Hurst, and White (2002) find that households
5:177:14105:10:0:72:540:72:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:are more likely to file for bankruptcy protection when there are larger financial benefits to doing so, and that there
6:178:14224:0:17:88:539:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Under Chapter 7, debtors forfeit all non-exempt assets in exchange for a discharge of eligible
6:179:14318:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:debts and protection from future wage garnishment.  Nearly all unsecured debts are eligible for
6:180:14413:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:discharge under Chapter 7, including credit card debt, installment loans, medical debt, unpaid rent
6:181:14512:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and utility bills, tort judgments, and business debt. Student loans, child support obligations, and
6:182:14611:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:debts incurred by fraud cannot be discharged under Chapter 7, and secured debts such as mortgages,
6:183:14709:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:home equity loans, and automobile loans can only be discharged if debtors give up the collateral. As
6:184:14809:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:most debtors have little non-exempt wealth or can move all non-exempt wealth into exempt assets
6:185:14904:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:before filing, the average repayment rate under Chapter 7 is only about one percent (Sullivan et
6:186:15000:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:al. 1989). Chapter 7 is chosen by the majority of filers in the United States, with 79.8 percent of
6:187:15099:16:17:72:276:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:debtors in our data filing under Chapter 7.
6:188:15142:17:16:88:539:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 7 cases begin with the debtor filing a bankruptcy petition, a statement of financial
6:189:15234:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:affairs, a copy of his or her most recent tax return, executory contracts and unexpired leases, and
6:190:15333:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:schedules of current income, expenditures, and assets and liabilities.  The assigned bankruptcy
6:191:15428:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:trustee then holds a meeting with the debtor to ensure that the debtor is aware of the potential
6:192:15524:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:adverse consequences of bankruptcy and to flag any potential issues for the bankruptcy judge. The
6:193:15621:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy judge will confirm or dismiss the application using the information from the filing and
6:194:15719:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the trustee’s report. If the filing is confirmed, the trustee liquidates the debtor’s property and splits
6:195:15824:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:it among the creditors. If the filing is dismissed, the debtor must exit the bankruptcy system and
6:196:15922:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:may not refile under either chapter for at least six years. In our data, 98.4 percent of Chapter 7
6:197:16020:17:16:72:256:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filings ending with a discharge of debt.
6:198:16060:16:17:88:539:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Under Chapter 13, filers propose a three- to five-year plan to repay part of their unsecured debt in
6:199:16160:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:exchange for a discharge of the remaining unsecured debt, protection from future wage garnishment,
6:200:16258:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and protection of most assets. For example, Chapter 13 allows debtors to retain assets pledged as
6:201:16355:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:collateral by including the collateral amount in the repayment plan. Chapter 13 also allows debtors
6:202:16454:17:16:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to avoid home foreclosure by including any mortgage arrears in the repayment plan, with the original
6:203:16554:16:17:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mortgage reinstated after completion of the plan. Seventy percent of dismissed Chapter 13 filers
6:204:16650:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:report that avoiding foreclosure is their principal reason for choosing to file under Chapter 13 (Porter
6:205:16754:16:17:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2011), with 71 percent of filers from a sample of Delaware cases including mortgage arrears in their
6:206:16854:17:16:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:repayment plans, 41 percent including car loans, and 38 percent including priority debt (White and
6:207:16952:16:17:72:123:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Zhu 2010).
6:208:16962:17:16:88:539:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 13 cases begin with the debtor filing a repayment plan and the paperwork described
6:209:17052:16:16:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:above. After a meeting between the debtor and bankruptcy trustee, the bankruptcy judge decides
6:210:17146:16:17:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whether the repayment plan is feasible and meets the standards for confirmation set forth in the
6:211:17242:17:16:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Bankruptcy Code.3If the judge confirms the repayment plan, the debtor makes regular payments
6:212:17334:16:35:71:539:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to the trustee until the plan is complete. The judge may dismiss or convert the case to Chapter 7 if
6:213:17434:35:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:is little impact of adverse shocks such as unemployment or divorce of the filing after conditioning on the financial
6:214:17550:11:7:72:106:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:benefits.
6:215:17559:7:15:87:539:97:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:3There is typically one Chapter 13 bankruptcy trustee that works with all judges in an office. If an office has
6:216:17670:15:11:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:a particularly high Chapter 13 caseload, judges may have their own Chapter 13 trustee.  Chapter 7 trustees are
6:217:17780:11:0:72:391:71:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:randomly assigned in a process that is independent from the judge assignment.
7:218:17858:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the debtor fails to make any payments, fails to pay any post-filing domestic support obligations, or
7:219:17958:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:fails to make required tax filings during the case. In our data, 48.8 percent of Chapter 13 filings end
7:220:18061:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with a discharge of debt. If a Chapter 13 filing is dismissed, debtors may refile for either Chapter 7
7:221:18163:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:or Chapter 13 after only 180 days. While almost no dismissed Chapter 13 filers in our sample refile
7:222:18262:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:under Chapter 13, approximately 20 percent choose to refile under Chapter 7. Thus, we estimate the
7:223:18360:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:impact of receiving Chapter 13 protection relative to both no bankruptcy protection and protection
7:224:18458:16:32:72:504:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:via Chapter 7. All of our estimates should be interpreted with this counterfactual in mind.
7:225:18549:32:23:240:371:578:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B. U.S. Bankruptcy Courts
7:226:18574:23:17:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There are 94 Federal bankruptcy courts in the United States, with at least one court in each state,
7:227:18673:17:16:72:540:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the District of Columbia, and Puerto Rico. Each bankruptcy court hears all cases originating from
7:228:18770:16:17:72:540:522:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:counties in its jurisdiction. Bankruptcy courts are often further divided into offices that hear all
7:229:18870:17:16:72:540:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:cases originating from a subset of counties in the court’s jurisdiction. Appendix Figure 1 displays
7:230:18969:16:16:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the 72 courts and 205 offices that we have data for. The median court in our sample is divided into
7:231:19068:16:17:72:457:473:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:three offices, with little systematic pattern to the number of offices in each office.
7:232:19154:17:16:88:539:456:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Bankruptcy judges are appointed to fourteen-year terms by the court of appeals in their judicial
7:233:19250:16:17:72:540:440:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:district. Bankruptcy judges only hear cases filed in their court, but often hear cases across multiple
7:234:19352:17:16:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:offices within their court. Within each bankruptcy office, cases are typically assigned to judges using
7:235:19455:16:17:72:335:407:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a random number generator or a blind rotation system.
7:236:19508:17:16:88:539:390:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The assigned bankruptcy judge decides any and all matters connected to a case, including
7:237:19596:16:16:72:540:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whether or not to dismiss the filing.  The most common reason a filing is dismissed is that it
7:238:19690:16:17:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:constitutes a “substantial abuse” of the bankruptcy process, typically meaning that a debtor should
7:239:19789:17:16:72:540:341:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:be able to repay his or her debts without bankruptcy protection. Other common reasons for dismissal
7:240:19888:16:17:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:include a filing missing important information, a Chapter 13 repayment plan being infeasible, or a
7:241:19986:17:16:72:540:308:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 13 repayment plan being too small (Hynes 2004). In Section IV, we discuss how we use
7:242:20078:16:17:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:systematic differences in the probability that a judge dismisses a filing to estimate the causal impact
7:243:20181:17:16:72:540:275:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of bankruptcy protection. These measured differences in judge behavior are likely to be the result
7:244:20279:16:17:72:540:259:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of differences in how judges interpret the criteria listed above, implying that more lenient judges
7:245:20378:17:16:72:494:242:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:may confirm repayment plans that are more generous to debtors or that are less feasible.
7:246:20466:16:16:88:539:226:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Despite the pivotal role of bankruptcy judges, debtors typically have only limited involvement
7:247:20560:16:17:72:540:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with the assigned judge. Chapter 7 filers do not appear before a judge unless a creditor or trustee
7:248:20659:17:16:72:540:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:raises an objection. Chapter 13 filers appear before the bankruptcy judge at the plan confirma-
7:249:20754:16:17:72:540:177:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tion hearing, but all other administrative aspects of the bankruptcy process are conducted by the
7:250:20851:17:16:72:294:160:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy trustee, not the bankruptcy judge.
7:251:20896:16:17:88:539:144:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There is considerable variation in the number of bankruptcy judges in each bankruptcy court
7:252:20987:17:16:72:540:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and office, with courts serving more populous regions tending to have more judges. Appendix Figure
7:253:21085:16:16:72:540:111:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1 displays the number of Chapter 13 bankruptcy judges in each office that we have data for. Of the
7:254:21183:16:17:72:540:95:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:205 offices in our sample, 110 have only one Chapter 13 judge, 52 have two Chapter 13 judges, 25
7:255:21279:17:0:72:431:78:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:have three Chapter 13 judges, and 18 have four or more Chapter 13 judges.
8:256:21353:0:23:193:419:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:C. Potential Benefits of Bankruptcy Protection
8:257:21399:23:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There are at least two reasons debtors may benefit from bankruptcy protection. First, bankruptcy
8:258:21495:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection may maintain the incentive to work by protecting future wages from garnishment. Wage
8:259:21590:16:17:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:garnishments occur when an employer is compelled by a court order to withhold a portion of an
8:260:21683:17:16:72:540:635:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:employee’s earnings to repay a particular debt. Federal law limits the amount that may be garnished
8:261:21782:16:17:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in any one week to the lesser of 25 percent of weekly disposable earnings, or the amount by which
8:262:21879:17:16:72:540:602:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:weekly disposable earnings exceed 30 times the federal minimum wage. Creditors are therefore able
8:263:21976:16:17:72:540:586:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to garnish 25 percent of each additional dollar of earnings above 40 times the federal minimum
8:264:22070:17:16:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:wage, 100 percent of earnings between 30 and 40 times the federal minimum wage, and nothing
8:265:22161:16:16:72:540:553:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on earnings below 30 times the federal minimum wage.4Bankruptcy protection stops all current
8:266:22253:16:17:72:540:537:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:garnishment orders and prevents any future garnishment orders on discharged debt, increasing the
8:267:22349:17:16:72:540:520:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f3:marginal return to work. Consistent with this mechanism, the U.S. Supreme Court argued inLocal
8:268:22443:16:17:72:539:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f2:Loan Co.v.Hunt(1934) that eliminating these wage garnishments is “[o]ne of the primary purposes
8:269:22538:17:16:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the Bankruptcy Act,” as “[f]rom the viewpoint of the wage earner, there is little difference between
8:270:22641:16:17:72:322:471:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:not earning at all and earning wholly for a creditor.”
8:271:22695:17:16:88:539:454:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Second, bankruptcy protection may prevent economic instability. Creditors have a number of
8:272:22785:16:16:72:540:438:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:options to collect unpaid debts if a debtor has not filed for bankruptcy protection or after a case is
8:273:22887:16:17:72:540:422:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:dismissed, including the wage garnishment orders discussed above, collection letters or phone calls,
8:274:22987:17:16:72:540:405:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in-person visits at home or work, and the seizing of assets through a court order (Hynes, Dawsey,
8:275:23084:16:17:72:540:389:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Ausubel 2009). Debtors can make these collection efforts more difficult by ignoring collection
8:276:23182:17:16:72:540:372:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:letters and calls, changing their telephone number, or moving without leaving a forwarding address.
8:277:23281:16:17:72:540:356:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Debtors can also leave the formal banking system to hide their assets from seizure, change jobs to
8:278:23379:17:16:72:540:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:force creditors to reinstate a garnishment order, or work less so that their earnings are not subject
8:279:23480:16:16:72:540:323:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to garnishment. Thus, bankruptcy protection may prevent economic instability by helping debtors
8:280:23575:16:17:72:540:307:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:avoid the kinds of sharp drops in consumption that have important long-term consequences, such as
8:281:23672:17:16:72:540:290:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:losing one’s home through foreclosure or becoming sick due to the lack of medical care. Bankruptcy
8:282:23770:16:17:72:540:274:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection may also reduce the incentive to strategically move across state lines or change jobs to
8:283:23869:17:16:72:145:257:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:avoid creditors.
8:284:23885:16:17:88:539:241:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There are also many reasons to believe that bankruptcy protection will have little impact on
8:285:23977:17:16:72:540:224:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:debtors. It is possible that financially distressed households have highly inelastic labor supply, or
8:286:24078:16:17:72:540:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that debt relief will reduce the incentive to work through the income effect. It is also possible that
8:287:24180:17:16:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:debtors are able to avoid most debt collection efforts at a relatively low cost, or that garnishment
8:288:24280:16:16:72:540:175:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:amounts are too low to impact labor supply decisions. Finally, it is possible that many bankruptcy
8:289:24378:16:17:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers are in financial distress due to low human capital or poor health that the bankruptcy system
8:290:24477:17:45:72:168:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is unable to remedy.
8:291:24497:45:15:87:539:97:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:4Federal law allows garnishments of up to 50 percent of a debtor’s disposable earnings for payment related to
8:292:24606:15:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:child support or alimony if the worker is supporting another spouse or child, and up to 60 percent if the worker is
8:293:24721:10:0:72:502:72:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:not. An additional five percent may be garnished for court order payments more than 12 weeks in arrears.
9:294:24826:0:28:281:330:708:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:II. Data
9:295:24834:28:16:72:540:680:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:To estimate the impact of bankruptcy protection on debtors, we merge information from individual
9:296:24930:16:16:72:540:664:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy filings, administrative tax records from the Social Security Administration (SSA), and
9:297:25027:16:17:72:396:648:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:proprietary real estate records from the data aggregator DataQuick.
9:298:25094:17:16:88:539:631:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Bankruptcy records are available from 1992 to 2009 for the 72 federal bankruptcy courts that
9:299:25186:16:17:72:540:615:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:allow full electronic access to their dockets. These data represent approximately three quarters of
9:300:25285:17:16:72:540:598:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:all bankruptcy filings during this period. Each record in our bankruptcy data contains information
9:301:25383:16:17:72:540:582:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on the Chapter filed, filing date, court, office, outcome, the judge and trustee assigned to each
9:302:25480:17:16:72:540:565:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filing, whether the filing includes any assets, and whether the filing fee was paid immediately or
9:303:25578:16:16:72:540:549:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in installments. The data also contain information on each debtor’s name, address, and last four
9:304:25674:16:17:72:289:533:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:digits of each debtor’s social security number.
9:305:25721:17:16:88:539:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We make five restrictions to our estimation sample. First, we drop 110 offices that only have
9:306:25814:16:17:72:540:500:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a single Chapter 13 bankruptcy judge, as there is no variation in judge leniency that allows us to
9:307:25912:17:16:72:540:483:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimate the impact of Chapter 13 protection. Second, we drop all filings originating from counties
9:308:26011:16:17:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that assign all cases to a single judge, as these filings are not randomly assigned. Third, we drop
9:309:26110:17:16:72:540:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:office by year bins where a retiring judge’s cases were reassigned with no documentation as to the
9:310:26208:16:17:72:540:434:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:original judge. Fourth, we drop office by year by judge bins with fewer than ten cases. Finally, we
9:311:26307:17:16:72:540:417:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:restrict the sample to first-time filers between 1992 and 2005 to ensure that we have five or more
9:312:26405:16:16:72:540:401:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:years of post-filing outcomes for all debtors and that all filings occurred before the 2005 Bankruptcy
9:313:26507:16:17:72:209:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Reform Act came into effect.
9:314:26535:17:16:88:539:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:These sample restrictions leave us with 534,980 Chapter 13 filings in 42 offices and 31 bankruptcy
9:315:26633:16:17:72:540:352:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:courts. These data represent just over 26 percent of the available Chapter 13 filings in the analysis
9:316:26734:17:16:72:540:335:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:period. The final sample includes 314 office by year observations, 112 office by judge observations,
9:317:26834:16:17:72:540:319:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and 758 office-year-judge observations. The number of cases in each office-year-judge bin ranges
9:318:26930:17:16:72:540:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:from 13 to 3,423. The median number of cases in each office-year-judge bin is 1,048. Appendix
9:319:27023:16:16:72:540:286:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 1 provides additional details on each of the offices in our estimation sample. Appendix Figures
9:320:27124:16:17:72:484:270:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:3 and 4 display the distribution of office-year-judge bins and office-year-judge leniency.
9:321:27214:17:16:88:539:253:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:To explore the impact of bankruptcy protection on subsequent labor supply and mortality, we
9:322:27305:16:17:72:540:237:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:matched the bankruptcy records to administrative tax records from the SSA. The SSA data are
9:323:27396:17:16:72:540:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:remarkably complete and include every individual who has ever acquired a SSN, including those
9:324:27489:16:17:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:who are institutionalized. Illegal immigrants without a valid SSN are not included in these data.
9:325:27586:17:16:72:540:187:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Information on earnings and employment comes from annual W-2s. Individuals with no W-2 in any
9:326:27679:16:17:72:540:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:particular year are assumed to have had no earnings in that year. Individuals with zero earnings
9:327:27775:17:16:72:540:154:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are included in all regressions throughout the paper. All dollar amounts are in terms of year 2000
9:328:27873:16:16:72:106:138:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:dollars.
9:329:27881:16:17:88:539:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We measure non-earnings outcomes using data from three sources. Information on annual 401k
9:330:27971:17:16:72:540:105:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:contributions, job location, and firm characteristics comes from annual W-2s. Information on DI
9:331:28066:16:17:72:540:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and SSI receipt comes from the Master Beneficiary Record. Information on mortality comes from
9:332:28159:17:0:72:540:72:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the Death Master File that is compiled by the SSA, and covers deaths occurring anywhere in the
10:333:28254:0:17:72:140:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:United States.
10:334:28268:17:16:88:539:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We match the bankruptcy data to the SSA records using last name and the last four digits of the
10:335:28363:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filer’s social security number. We were able to successfully match 91.6 percent of the bankruptcy
10:336:28460:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:records, with nearly all of the unmatched records resulting from a shared name and last four digits
10:337:28559:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the social security number in the SSA data. The probability of being matched to the SSA data
10:338:28654:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is not significantly related to judge leniency. Our estimation sample consists of the 490,216 filers in
10:339:28757:16:17:72:172:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the matched dataset.
10:340:28777:17:16:88:539:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:To explore the impact of bankruptcy protection on home foreclosures, we also matched the
10:341:28865:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy records to proprietary real estate data purchased from DataQuick.  The DataQuick
10:342:28956:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:files include information on the most recent county assessment, pre-foreclosure notices, and all
10:343:29052:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:home transactions.  The DataQuick files are compiled by county and year, with more complete
10:344:29143:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:coverage for more urban areas and more recent years. There are 280,202 Chapter 13 bankruptcy
10:345:29235:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers matched to the SSA data living in county by year bins covered by the DataQuick records. We
10:346:29332:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:matched these filers to the DataQuick records using last name and filing address. We were able
10:347:29426:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to successfully match 48.5 percent of filers to either a past home transaction or a current home
10:348:29522:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:assessment. In a random sample of approximately 3,000 Chapter 13 filings between 1999 and 2005,
10:349:29617:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Agarwal et al. (2010) find that 51 percent of Chapter 13 filers are homeowners, suggesting that we
10:350:29715:17:16:72:539:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are finding most homeowners in our data.5Importantly, the probability of being matched to the
10:351:29808:16:17:72:301:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:DataQuick data is not related to judge leniency.
10:352:29856:17:16:88:539:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 1 presents summary statistics for all first-time filers between 1992 and 2005 and our
10:353:29947:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimation sample of first-time filers randomly assigned to judges between 1992 and 2005. Consistent
10:354:30047:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with previous research on bankruptcy filers, 98.4 percent of Chapter 7 filers in our data are granted
10:355:30148:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy protection, compared to 48.8 percent of Chapter 13 filers. Sixty percent of Chapter 7
10:356:30244:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers are male, 74.2 percent are white, and 13.3 percent are black. For Chapter 13, 63.4 percent of
10:357:30344:17:16:72:385:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers are male, 55.8 percent are white, and 33.9 percent are black.
10:358:30412:16:17:88:539:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The typical bankruptcy filer earns far less than the average American worker. In the five years
10:359:30507:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:before filing, 80.6 percent of Chapter 7 filers are employed on average, with average annual earnings
10:360:30608:16:17:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of just $21,090. Eighty percent of Chapter 13 filers are employed, earning $22,333 annually in the
10:361:30706:17:16:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:five years before filing. Over the same five year time period, 4.7 percent of Chapter 7 filers receive
10:362:30808:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:DI, and 9.7 percent receive SSI. Just over four percent of Chapter 13 filers receive DI, and 8.4
10:363:30904:17:16:72:165:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:percent receive SSI.
10:364:30924:16:16:88:539:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Column 3 of Table 1 presents summary statistics for filers in our estimation sample.  The
10:365:31013:16:17:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimation sample is very similar to the full sample of filers.  Forty-four point eight percent of
10:366:31111:17:16:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 13 filers in our sample are granted bankruptcy protection, 4.0 percentage points less than
10:367:31209:16:31:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the full sample. Sixty point nine percent of filers in our sample are male, 2.5 percentage points less
10:368:31311:31:15:87:539:119:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:5Filers are classified as homeowners if they list real property on Schedule A of the bankruptcy form. The Chapter
10:369:31424:15:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:13 homeownership rate was provided directly by the authors. There is also evidence that the fraction of Chapter
10:370:31535:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:13 filers who are homeowners has increased in recent years. Lawless et al. (2008) find that 69.6 percent of Chapter
10:371:31650:11:11:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:13 filers are homeowners in a random sample of filers in 2007, with other, more selected survey samples suggesting
10:372:31764:11:0:72:523:71:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:homeownership rates of between 70 and 96 percent in the post-2005 period (White and Zhu 2010, Porter 2011).
11:373:31872:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:than the full sample. 401k contributions are also $33 per year higher in the estimation sample, while
11:374:31973:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:average firm wages are $3,874 higher. Conversely, filers in our estimation sample are statistically
11:375:32072:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:indistinguishable from the full sample with regard to age, ethnic background, employment, earnings,
11:376:32171:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:job tenure, the probability of being matched to a home in the DataQuick files, and the probability
11:377:32269:16:34:72:178:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of receiving DI or SSI.
11:378:32292:34:27:274:337:609:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:III. Model
11:379:32302:27:16:71:539:582:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In this section, we motivate our empirical analysis by describing a simple model of how consumer
11:380:32398:16:17:71:539:566:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy functions as a social insurance mechanism. The model illustrates the trade-off between
11:381:32495:17:16:71:539:549:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the consumption smoothing benefits provided by bankruptcy protection with the increased borrow-
11:382:32590:16:17:71:539:533:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ing costs that result from the higher risk of default. We then consider how the estimates of the
11:383:32686:17:31:71:500:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effect of bankruptcy protection on labor supply can shed light on those benefits and costs.
11:384:32777:31:24:222:389:485:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A. Bankruptcy as Social Insurance
11:385:32810:24:16:71:539:461:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Consider a continuum of risk averse agents who experience an expense shockπdistributedπ∼[π,π].
11:386:32904:16:17:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Each agent pays for the expense shock through an existing credit line at interest rater. We assume
11:387:33002:17:16:72:480:428:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f4:that agents borrow exactlyπand that there is a single interest rate for all all agents.6
11:388:33090:16:16:88:539:412:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Agents who are not eligible for bankruptcy protection repay(1+r)πto lenders. Agents who are
11:389:33181:16:17:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:eligible for bankruptcy protection repay(1+r)αbwl, whereαbwl < πfor all agents. We assume that
11:390:33275:17:16:72:540:379:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:there are no other direct or indirect costs of bankruptcy, and that all agents eligible for bankruptcy
11:391:33377:16:17:72:235:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection will file for bankruptcy.
11:392:33413:17:16:88:539:346:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f8:Each agent’s utility is defined asU(c)−ψ(l), where consumptioncequals wage earningswl
11:393:33498:16:17:72:540:330:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:minus debt repayment(1 +r)πor(1 +r)αbwl. We assume that U is concave andψis convex.
11:394:33581:17:16:72:540:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We begin with the assumption thatlis fixed for all agents to highlight the insurance aspects of
11:395:33676:16:16:72:540:297:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy protection. In the next section, we allow agents to choose labor supply to show how
11:396:33770:16:17:72:487:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy protection may impact earnings. We assume wagesware fixed throughout.
11:397:33850:17:16:88:539:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The lending market is perfectly competitive, leading to no profits in equilibrium. We normalize
11:398:33945:16:17:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the shadow cost of bank funds to zero so that the expected cost of lending equals the expected
11:399:34039:17:9:72:200:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f12:repayment amount:∫
11:400:34057:9:21:205:210:222:8:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f11:π
11:401:34058:21:0:200:205:201:8:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f11:π
11:402:34059:0:0:212:244:211:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f10:π dπ=
11:403:34064:0:25:248:268:226:11:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f13:∫π∗
11:404:34067:25:0:254:259:201:8:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f11:π
11:405:34068:0:0:265:328:211:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:(1 +r)π dπ+
11:406:34079:0:25:331:347:226:11:g_d0_f12:8:g_d0_f11:∫π
11:407:34081:25:0:337:347:201:8:g_d0_f11:6:g_d0_f13:π∗
11:408:34083:0:29:348:540:211:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f2:(1 +r)αbwldπ(1)
11:409:34098:29:16:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereπ∗is the cutoff for bankruptcy eligibility chosen by the social planner. Equation (1) yields
11:410:34195:16:25:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the familiar result that a more restrictive bankruptcy system decreases borrowing costs as more
11:411:34290:25:15:87:539:141:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:6The assumption that agents borrow exactlyπsimplifies the model without affecting the key results. We further
11:412:34399:15:11:72:540:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:simplify the model by assuming that agents only face expense risk that is unlikely to be covered by existing social
11:413:34514:11:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:insurance mechanisms, such as Unemployment Insurance. Our model is therefore unable to shed light on the interac-
11:414:34627:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:tion of bankruptcy protection and these other forms of social insurance. The derivation of an optimal social insurance
11:415:34745:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:system with conceptually distinct types of risk remains an important area for future work. See Jackson (1986) and
11:416:34858:11:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Posner (1995) for discussion of the relationship between bankruptcy and government safety net programs, and Rea
11:417:34969:10:0:72:457:72:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:(1984) for discussion of why private consumption insurance does not exist in the United States.
12:418:35065:0:25:72:236:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:individuals fully repay their debts:
12:419:35101:25:15:225:236:684:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:∂r
12:420:35103:15:0:222:239:669:11:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f14:∂π∗
12:421:35106:0:0:244:264:677:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f9:=−
12:422:35108:0:8:273:361:684:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:(1 +r)(π∗−αbwl)
12:423:35123:8:13:265:282:676:11:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f13:∫π∗
12:424:35126:13:0:271:312:663:8:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f10:ππ dπ+
12:425:35132:0:13:315:327:676:11:g_d0_f12:8:g_d0_f11:∫π
12:426:35134:13:0:320:368:663:8:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f8:π∗αbwldπ
12:427:35142:0:38:373:540:677:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:<0(2)
12:428:35147:38:16:71:539:639:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The sensitivity of borrowing costs to the bankruptcy eligibility cutoff is increasing in the difference
12:429:35250:16:16:71:540:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:between what creditors are repaid by the marginal non-filer and marginal filer(π∗−αbwl). This is
12:430:35346:16:17:71:539:607:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:because a larger change inris needed to compensate creditors for the lost revenue associated with
12:431:35443:17:16:71:539:590:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a more lenient bankruptcy cutoff when the difference in the amount repaid is large. Conversely,
12:432:35538:16:17:71:539:574:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the sensitivity of borrowing costs to the bankruptcy eligibility cutoff is decreasing in the expected
12:433:35639:17:0:71:162:557:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:repayment amount
12:434:35655:0:16:167:192:569:11:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f13:(∫π∗
12:435:35659:16:0:180:223:553:8:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f10:ππ dπ+
12:436:35665:0:13:226:239:566:11:g_d0_f12:8:g_d0_f11:∫π
12:437:35667:13:0:232:280:553:8:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f8:π∗αbwldπ
12:438:35675:0:12:280:287:569:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:)
12:439:35676:12:16:287:539:557:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:, as a smaller change inris needed to compensate
12:440:35724:16:17:71:539:541:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:creditors for the lost revenue associated with a more lenient bankruptcy cutoff when the total
12:441:35818:17:16:71:201:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:repayment amount is large.
12:442:35844:16:16:88:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The social planner chooses the bankruptcy eligibility cutoffπ∗, where agents are eligible for
12:443:35937:16:17:72:539:492:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy protection iffπ > π∗. Since all agents are identical ex-ante, the social welfare function
12:444:36037:17:19:71:405:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is the same as the representative consumer’s expected utility function:
12:445:36108:19:24:124:144:456:11:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f13:∫π∗
12:446:36111:24:0:130:135:432:8:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f11:π
12:447:36112:0:0:143:302:441:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f10:U(wl−(1 +r(π∗))π)−ψ(l)dπ+
12:448:36137:0:24:304:320:456:11:g_d0_f12:8:g_d0_f11:∫π
12:449:36139:24:0:311:320:432:8:g_d0_f11:6:g_d0_f13:π∗
12:450:36141:0:34:323:540:441:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:U(wl−(1 +r(π∗))αbwl)−ψ(l)dπ(3)
12:451:36171:34:16:71:539:407:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The first order condition for equation (3) equates the benefit of bankruptcy protection for the
12:452:36266:16:21:71:389:391:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:marginal recipient with the marginal cost of providing bankruptcy:
12:453:36332:21:12:81:88:370:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:(
12:454:36333:12:0:88:218:358:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f10:U(wl−(1 +r)αbwl)−ψ(l)
12:455:36354:0:12:218:225:370:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:)
12:456:36355:12:0:227:235:358:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:−
12:457:36356:0:12:238:245:370:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:(
12:458:36357:12:0:244:363:358:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f10:U(wl−(1 +r)π∗)−ψ(l)
12:459:36376:0:12:363:370:370:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:)
12:460:36377:12:30:373:381:358:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:=
12:461:36378:30:0:173:181:328:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:−
12:462:36379:0:15:188:199:335:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:∂r
12:463:36381:15:0:185:202:320:11:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f14:∂π∗
12:464:36384:0:7:206:220:347:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:(∫
12:465:36386:7:22:225:235:340:8:g_d0_f11:6:g_d0_f13:π∗
12:466:36388:22:0:221:226:318:8:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f11:π
12:467:36389:0:0:234:349:328:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f10:πUc(wl−(1 +r)π)dπ+
12:468:36407:0:25:352:368:343:11:g_d0_f12:8:g_d0_f11:∫π
12:469:36409:25:0:358:367:318:8:g_d0_f11:6:g_d0_f13:π∗
12:470:36411:0:0:370:507:328:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:αbwlUc(wl−(1 +r)αbwl)dπ
12:471:36434:0:19:507:516:347:11:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f12:)
12:472:36435:19:35:526:540:328:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(4)
12:473:36438:35:17:72:397:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereUcindicates the first derivatives with respect to consumption.
12:474:36505:17:16:88:539:276:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Equation (4) highlights the trade-off between the consumption smoothing benefits provided by
12:475:36597:16:17:72:539:260:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy protection when shocks are large (π > π∗) and the increased costs of self-insurance
12:476:36691:17:16:72:539:243:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:when shocks are small (π < π∗). This trade-off is at the heart of an important literature measuring
12:477:36790:16:17:72:540:227:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the effect of consumer bankruptcy on welfare using quantitative models of the credit market (e.g.
12:478:36887:17:16:72:540:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Athreya 2002, Li and Sarte 2006, Livshits, MacGee, and Tertilt 2007, Chatterjee and Gordon
12:479:36977:16:17:72:540:194:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2012). An important limitation of this literature has been the lack of empirical evidence on the
12:480:37073:17:16:72:540:177:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:magnitude of both the benefits provided by bankruptcy protection for the marginal recipient and
12:481:37168:16:16:72:540:161:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the costs associated with more expensive borrowing. There is also relatively little information on the
12:482:37270:16:17:72:540:145:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mechanisms through which bankruptcy protection benefits debtors, forcing the previous literature
12:483:37366:17:16:72:540:128:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to make strong assumptions, such as abstracting away from the production side of the economy (e.g.
12:484:37464:16:17:72:540:112:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Athreya 2002, Livshits, MacGee, and Tertilt 2007), assuming that labor supply is only influenced
12:485:37560:17:16:72:540:95:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by the aggregate capital stock (e.g. Li and Sarte 2006), or assuming that labor supply is extremely
12:486:37659:16:0:72:282:79:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:inelastic (e.g. Chatterjee and Gordon 2012).
13:487:37705:0:23:225:386:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B. Bankruptcy and Labor Supply
13:488:37735:23:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Next, we consider how estimates of the impact of bankruptcy protection on labor supply shed
13:489:37826:17:16:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:light on the benefits and costs of the consumer bankruptcy system as described by equation (4).
13:490:37921:16:17:72:540:652:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In the simple setup described above, bankruptcy protection unambiguously decreases labor supply
13:491:38016:17:16:72:540:635:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:through both substitution and wealth effects. However, the assumption that agents fully repay their
13:492:38115:16:17:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:debts outside of the bankruptcy system is unlikely to hold in practice given that the majority of
13:493:38212:17:16:72:540:602:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:debt write-offs occur outside of the bankruptcy system (Hynes, Dawsey, and Ausubel 2009). We
13:494:38304:16:17:72:540:586:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:therefore make the more realistic assumption that agents who do not receive bankruptcy protection
13:495:38401:17:16:72:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:default on their debt and are subject to wage garnishment at rateαg. The wage garnishment rate
13:496:38495:16:16:72:539:553:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is assumed to be larger than the bankruptcy repayment rateαg> αb, implying that bankruptcy
13:497:38585:16:17:72:540:537:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection reduces the implicit tax on earnings associated with default. We also assume that the
13:498:38681:17:16:72:539:520:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:amount repaid through garnishment(1 +r)αgwlis less than the amount borrowedπfor all agents.
13:499:38772:16:30:88:450:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Each agent’s labor supply is described by the following first order condition:
13:500:38850:30:30:197:540:474:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:w(1−(1 +r)α)·Ul(wl(1−(1 +r)α)) =ψl(l)(5)
13:501:38890:30:16:71:540:444:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereUlandψlindicate first derivatives with respect to labor supply, andαis the implicit tax on
13:502:38985:16:17:71:539:428:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:earnings associated with either wage garnishment or bankruptcy. Equation (5) yields the familiar
13:503:39081:17:16:71:540:411:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:result that a reduction in the implicit tax rateαthrough bankruptcy protection has an ambiguous
13:504:39176:16:26:71:413:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:impact on labor supply due to opposing substitution and wealth effects:
13:505:39247:26:14:146:156:369:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:∂l
13:506:39249:14:0:144:157:355:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:∂α
13:507:39251:0:0:162:170:362:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:=
13:508:39252:0:14:211:262:369:11:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:(1 +r)wUl
13:509:39261:14:0:174:299:355:11:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:[(1−(1 +r)α)w]2Ull−ψll
13:510:39283:0:0:303:311:362:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:+
13:511:39284:0:14:315:446:369:11:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:(1 +r)(1−(1 +r)α)w2lUlα
13:512:39307:14:0:319:443:355:11:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f11:[(1−(1 +r)α)w]2Ull−ψll
13:513:39329:0:32:451:540:362:11:g_d0_f17:11:g_d0_f2:≶0(6)
13:514:39334:32:16:72:540:330:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Thus, bankruptcy protection increases the earnings of the marginal recipient if the substitution
13:515:39430:16:17:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effect associated with the reduced tax on earnings dominates. Conversely, bankruptcy protection
13:516:39525:17:16:72:540:297:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:decreases the earnings of the marginal recipient if the marginal non-recipient is not subject to wage
13:517:39626:16:17:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:garnishment or the wealth effect dominates. The effect of bankruptcy protection on labor supply is
13:518:39724:17:16:72:222:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:therefore an empirical question.
13:519:39756:16:17:88:539:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Labor supply estimates for the marginal recipient of bankruptcy protection influence the benefits
13:520:39853:17:16:72:540:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and costs of the consumer bankruptcy system in at least two ways. First, any labor supply response
13:521:39951:16:16:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:will change the consumption smoothing benefits provided by bankruptcy protection. If bankruptcy
13:522:40046:16:17:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection increases the marginal recipient’s earnings, the difference between consumption of the
13:523:40143:17:16:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:marginal filer and marginal non-filer is increased, as are the consumption smoothing benefits of
13:524:40239:16:17:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy protection. The reverse holds if bankruptcy has a negative impact on debtor earnings.
13:525:40335:17:16:72:540:149:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Second, any labor supply response will change the sensitivity of borrowing costs to bankruptcy
13:526:40429:16:17:72:540:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:policy and the costs associated with bankruptcy protection.  If bankruptcy protection increases
13:527:40524:17:16:72:540:116:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the marginal recipient’s earnings, the difference in the amount repaid to creditors by the marginal
13:528:40623:16:16:72:540:100:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filer and marginal non-filer is reduced, decreasing the sensitivity of borrowing costs to bankruptcy
13:529:40723:16:0:72:540:84:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:policy and lowering the cost of the bankruptcy system. The reverse again holds if bankruptcy has
14:530:40821:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a negative impact on debtor earnings. Thus, a positive (negative) impact of bankruptcy protection
14:531:40918:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on earnings suggests that the bankruptcy system has larger (smaller) benefits and smaller (larger)
14:532:41016:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:costs than implied by models with inelastic labor supply (e.g. Athreya 2002, Livshits, MacGee, and
14:533:41114:17:33:72:280:659:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f4:Tertilt 2007, Chatterjee and Gordon 2012).7
14:534:41157:33:27:244:366:626:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:IV. Research Design
14:535:41176:27:30:71:517:599:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Consider a model that relates post-filing outcomes such as earnings to bankruptcy protection:
14:536:41269:30:30:220:540:569:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:yit=α+βXi+γBankruptcyi+εit(7)
14:537:41298:30:16:71:539:539:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereidenotes individuals,tis the year of observation,γis the causal impact of bankruptcy
14:538:41387:16:17:71:539:523:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection,Xiincludes controls such as race and gender, andεitis noise. The problem for inference
14:539:41484:17:16:71:540:506:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is that OLS estimates ofγmay be biased if bankruptcy protection is correlated with the unobservable
14:540:41583:16:17:71:540:490:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:determinants of later outcomes:E[εit|Bankruptcyi]6= 0. For example, the most proximate causes
14:541:41676:17:16:71:539:473:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of bankruptcy, such as job loss and health shocks, may also impact later outcomes, biasing both
14:542:41771:16:16:71:539:457:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:cross-sectional (e.g. Han and Li 2007, 2011) and within-individual (e.g. Cohen-Cole, Duygan-Bump
14:543:41867:16:17:71:333:441:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Montoriol-Garriga 2009) estimates of equation (7).
14:544:41921:17:16:88:540:424:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We identify the causal impact of bankruptcy on debtorsγusing judge leniency as an instrument
14:545:42013:16:17:71:539:408:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for bankruptcy protection. Intuitively, we compare the post-filings outcomes of debtors assigned
14:546:42109:17:16:71:539:391:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to bankruptcy judges that have different propensities to grant Chapter 13 protection, interpreting
14:547:42207:16:17:71:539:375:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:any differences as a causal effect of the change in the probability of receiving bankruptcy protection
14:548:42309:17:16:71:235:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:associated with these propensities.
14:549:42344:16:16:88:539:342:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Formally, we estimate the causal impact of receiving bankruptcy protection through a two-stage
14:550:42438:16:17:71:539:326:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:least squares regression using judge leniency as an instrumental variable for bankruptcy protection.
14:551:42538:17:30:71:264:309:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The second stage estimating equation is:
14:552:42578:30:29:206:540:279:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:yit=α+αot+βXi+γBankruptcyi+εit(8)
14:553:42611:29:17:71:540:250:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereαotare office by month-of-filing fixed effects andXiincludes race, gender, five-year age effects,
14:554:42713:17:16:71:539:233:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a five-year average of baseline employment, and a five-year average of baseline earnings. The first
14:555:42812:16:30:71:345:217:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:stage estimating equation associated with equation (8) is:
14:556:42870:30:24:205:540:187:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:Bankruptcyit=α+αot+βXi+δσj+εit(9)
14:557:42903:24:15:87:539:163:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:7In a model with endogenous borrowing, the consumer bankruptcy system increases loan demand through lower
14:558:43008:15:11:72:540:148:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:costs of default and improved risk sharing. Borrowing distortions from the lower costs of default are likely increasing
14:559:43127:11:11:72:540:137:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:with the benefits of filing for bankruptcy protection. As the benefits of bankruptcy protection are increasing with
14:560:43242:11:11:72:540:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:the magnitude of the labor supply estimates, the distortions to borrowing behavior are also likely to be increasing
14:561:43357:11:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:with the magnitude of the labor supply estimates. Severino, Brown, and Coates (2014) provide more direct evidence
14:562:43470:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:on this issue using within-state variation in asset exemptions, finding that increased protection under the Chapter
14:563:43585:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:7 bankruptcy system increases unsecured borrowing without increasing the probability of default.  These results
14:564:43696:11:11:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:are consistent with the consumer bankruptcy system increasing borrowing through improved risk sharing, without
14:565:43806:11:0:72:381:71:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:significantly increasing the prevalence of adverse selection and moral hazard.
15:566:43886:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereσjis the systematic component of judge behavior andδrepresents the impact of that judge
15:567:43978:17:16:71:539:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:behavior on the probability of receiving bankruptcy protection. To account for any serial correlation
15:568:44079:16:17:71:539:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:across filers at the level of randomization, we cluster standard errors at the office level in both the
15:569:44182:17:16:71:539:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:first and second stage regressions. Results are qualitatively similar if we cluster at the office by
15:570:44282:16:17:71:254:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:judge or office by month-of-filing level.
15:571:44323:17:16:88:539:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Using an exhaustive set of judge fixed effects as an instrument for bankruptcy protection yields
15:572:44419:16:17:71:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a consistent two-stage least squares estimate ofγas the number of filersi→∞, but is potentially
15:573:44514:17:16:71:539:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:biased in finite samples.  This bias is the result of the mechanical correlation between a filer’s
15:574:44612:16:16:71:539:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:own outcomes and the estimation of that filer’s judge fixed effects.  There are several potential
15:575:44709:16:17:71:539:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:solutions to this own-observation issue. Jackknife IV eliminates the bias by omitting a filer’s own
15:576:44808:17:16:71:539:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:observation when forming the instrument (Angrist, Imbens, and Krueger 1999). Split-sample two-
15:577:44902:16:17:71:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:stage IV addresses the own-observation issue by randomly splitting the sample into two groups,
15:578:44996:17:16:71:539:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:using judge tendencies in one part of the sample as an instrument for bankruptcy protection in the
15:579:45094:16:17:71:539:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:other part of the sample (Angrist and Krueger 1995). Limited information maximum likelihood
15:580:45185:17:16:71:539:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(LIML) eliminates the own-observation bias by collapsing the parameter space and using maximum
15:581:45279:16:16:71:451:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:likelihood to obtain a consistent estimate of the effect of bankruptcy protection.
15:582:45361:16:17:88:539:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We address the own-observation problem by using a leave-one-out measure of judge leniency as
15:583:45453:17:16:71:539:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:an instrument for bankruptcy protection (Kling 2006, Chang and Schoar 2008, Doyle 2007, 2008,
15:584:45546:16:17:71:539:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Autor and Houseman 2010, French and Song 2011, Aizer and Doyle 2013, Maestas, Mullen, and
15:585:45635:17:16:71:539:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Strand 2013). Our measure of judge leniencyZicjtis defined as the leave-one-out fraction of filings
15:586:45734:16:36:71:513:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:granted by judgejin yeartminus the leave-one-out fraction granted in his courtcin yeart:
15:587:45822:36:0:162:195:344:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f10:Zicjt=
15:588:45828:0:15:215:220:351:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:1

15:590:45835:0:9:239:263:363:11:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f18:(ncjt

15:603:45875:19:36:520:539:344:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(10)
15:604:45879:36:17:71:540:308:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereiagain denotes individuals,cdenotes courts,jis the assigned judge,tis the year of obser-
15:605:45972:17:16:71:540:291:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:vation,Biis an indicator for receiving bankruptcy protection,ncjtis the number of cases seen by
15:606:46067:16:17:71:539:275:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a judge in yeart, andnctis the number of cases seen by a court in yeart. This leave-one-out pro-
15:607:46163:17:16:71:539:258:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:cedure is essentially a reduced-form version of jackknife IV that purges the mechanical correlation
15:608:46262:16:17:71:540:242:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:between a filer’s own outcomes and our measure of judge leniency.8Following the literature (Kling
15:609:46359:17:16:71:539:225:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2006, Chang and Schoar 2008, Doyle 2007, 2008, Autor and Houseman 2010, French and Song 2011,
15:610:46452:16:16:71:539:209:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Aizer and Doyle 2013, Maestas, Mullen, and Strand 2013), we do not adjust our standard errors to
15:611:46548:16:17:71:325:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:account for the fact that the instrument is estimated.
15:612:46602:17:16:88:539:176:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Consistent with past research (Sullivan, Warren, and Westbrook 1994, Norberg and Compo
15:613:46688:16:17:71:539:160:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2007), we find considerable variation in the treatment of Chapter 13 cases within an office. The
15:614:46784:17:16:71:540:143:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:standard deviation ofZijctis 0.030 for Chapter 13 filers in our sample. There is also significant
15:615:46881:16:30:71:539:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:persistence in our measure of judge behavior. Appendix Figure 4 plots current and lagged judge
15:616:46975:30:15:87:539:97:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:8Appendix Table 2 presents two-stage least squares, LIML, and Jackknife IV results using judge fixed effects as
15:617:47086:15:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:instruments for bankruptcy protection. The results are qualitatively similar to our preferred estimates presented in
15:618:47202:10:0:72:105:72:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Table 4.
16:619:47212:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:discharge rates, with each point representing a separate judge by year observation. Discharge rates
16:620:47311:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are highly correlated across time, with an OLS regression relating each judge by year discharge
16:621:47406:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:rate to the lagged discharge rate yielding a coefficient of 0.814. These results suggest that we are
16:622:47506:17:16:72:462:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:capturing systematic differences in judge behavior, not random year to year noise.
16:623:47588:16:17:88:539:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In contrast to Chapter 13, there is almost no variation in the treatment of Chapter 7 cases across
16:624:47686:17:16:72:539:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:judges within an office. The standard deviation ofZijctfor Chapter 7 filers is only 0.003 in our
16:625:47782:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:data, likely because almost all Chapter 7 filings are granted. This lack of variation makes it difficult
16:626:47886:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to measure the effect of Chapter 7 bankruptcy protection using our instrumental variables strategy.
16:627:47985:16:16:72:522:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In Section VE, we use an event study strategy to estimate the impact of Chapter 7 protection.
16:628:48078:16:17:88:540:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Using our reduced form measure of judge leniencyZijctas an instrument for the receipt of
16:629:48166:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection, the identified two-stage least squares parameter from equation
16:630:48262:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(8) measures the local average treatment effect of Chapter 13 for filers whose bankruptcy outcomes
16:631:48360:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are altered by judge assignment. The conditions necessary to interpret these two-stage least squares
16:632:48460:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimates as the causal impact of Chapter 13 protection are: (1) that judge assignment is associated
16:633:48560:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with bankruptcy protection, (2) that judge assignment only impacts debtor outcomes through the
16:634:48654:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:probability of receiving bankruptcy protection, and (3) that the impact of judge assignment on the
16:635:48752:16:17:72:416:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:probability of receiving bankruptcy protection is monotonic across filers.
16:636:48826:17:16:88:539:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The first assumption is empirically testable. Figure 1 plots average discharge vs. our leave-
16:637:48919:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:one-out measure of judge leniency. The estimation sample includes first-time filers between 1992
16:638:49015:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and 2005 in the 42 offices in the 31 courts that randomly assign Chapter 13 filings to judges.
16:639:49109:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:To construct the plot, we calculate mean residuals from a regression of an indicator for receiving
16:640:49207:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 13 protection on office by month-of-filing fixed effects. We then add the mean discharge rate
16:641:49308:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to the mean residual in each judge by year bin to aid in the interpretation of the scale. The resulting
16:642:49411:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:scatter plot provides a non-parametric representation of the conditional expectation function, but
16:643:49509:17:16:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:does not show the underlying variance in the individual-level data. The solid line and corresponding
16:644:49609:16:17:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:coefficient show the best linear fit estimated on the underlying individual-level data, controlling for
16:645:49712:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:office by month-of-filing fixed effects and with standard errors clustered at the office level. Table 2
16:646:49815:16:17:72:465:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presents analogous individual-level estimates with and without additional controls.
16:647:49898:17:16:88:539:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:First stage results from Figure 1 and Table 2 show a large and precisely estimated relationship
16:648:49993:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:between judge leniency and the probability of receiving bankruptcy protection. With no filer level
16:649:50091:17:16:72:539:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:controls, a one percentage point increase inZijctincreases the probability that a debtor receives
16:650:50188:16:16:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy protection by 0.749 percentage points. Controlling for gender, race, age, and baseline
16:651:50285:16:17:72:539:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:earnings, a one percentage point increase inZijctincreases the probability that a debtor receives
16:652:50382:17:16:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy protection by 0.731 percentage points. Thus, a one standard deviation (three percentage
16:653:50480:16:17:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:point) increase in judge leniency increases the likelihood of receiving Chapter 13 bankruptcy protec-
16:654:50581:17:16:72:540:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tion by about 2.2 percentage points, a 4.9 percent change from the mean. To put these magnitudes
