16:655:50677:16:17:72:540:117:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in perspective, black filers are 9.0 percentage points less likely to receive bankruptcy protection, a
16:656:50779:17:16:72:540:100:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:one year younger filer is 0.5 percentage points less likely, and filers with baseline earnings that are
16:657:50882:16:0:72:346:84:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:$10,000 lower are about 0.05 percentage points less likely.
17:658:50943:0:17:88:539:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The probability of receiving Chapter 13 protection does not increase one-for-one with our mea-
17:659:51037:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:sure of judge leniency, likely because of measurement error that attenuates the effect toward zero.
17:660:51136:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For instance, judge leniency may drift over the course of the year or fluctuate with case character-
17:661:51236:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:istics, reducing the accuracy of our leave-one-out measure. Nevertheless, the results from Figure 1
17:662:51335:16:17:72:442:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Table 2 confirm that judge leniency is highly predictive of case outcomes.
17:663:51413:17:16:88:539:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our second identifying assumption is that judge assignment only impacts debtor outcomes
17:664:51500:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:through the probability of receiving bankruptcy protection.  This assumption would be violated
17:665:51594:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:if judge leniency is correlated with unobservable determinants of future outcomes. Table 3 presents
17:666:51693:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a series of randomization checks to partially assess the validity of this exclusion restriction. Column
17:667:51796:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2 reports results from an OLS regression of judge leniency on a filer’s age, gender, race, an indicator
17:668:51899:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for being matched to a home at baseline, and baseline earnings, employment, self-employment earn-
17:669:51996:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ings, self-employment, 401k contributions, receipt of Disability Insurance, job tenure, and average
17:670:52095:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:employer wages. Each baseline measure is the average over the five years before filing. We control
17:671:52193:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for office by month-of-filing fixed effects, and cluster standard errors at the office level. Job tenure is
17:672:52300:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:associated with judge leniency at the ten percent level. None of our other baseline variables are sig-
17:673:52402:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:nificantly related to judge leniency, and a joint F-test of the hypothesis that all baseline differences
17:674:52506:16:17:72:261:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are equal to zero has a p-value of 0.233.
17:675:52547:17:16:88:539:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Columns 3 adds controls for predicted earnings, employment, and mortality. We predict each
17:676:52637:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:outcome over the first five post-filing years using gender, race, five-year age effects, and employment
17:677:52740:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and earnings in the sixth through tenth years before bankruptcy. Job tenure is the only significant
17:678:52839:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:measures, and a joint F-test that all the baseline differences listed in column 3 are equal to zero has
17:679:52942:17:16:72:162:363:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f4:a p-value of 0.252.9
17:680:52962:16:16:88:539:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Column 4 presents results from our final test of random assignment. We regress each baseline
17:681:53054:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:measure on an exhaustive set of judge fixed effects. Each regression controls for office by month-
17:682:53152:17:16:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of-filing fixed effects. We report the p-value from a joint F-test that the judge effects are jointly
17:683:53253:16:17:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:different than zero, which provides an omnibus test for the null hypothesis that filer covariates do not
17:684:53357:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:differ significantly among filers assigned to judges within an office by month-of-filing combination.
17:685:53458:16:17:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The joint F-test for age has a p-value of 0.051. None of the other joint F-tests in column 4 suggest
17:686:53558:17:16:72:394:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that there is systematic non-random assignment of filings to judges.
17:687:53626:16:17:88:539:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The exclusion restriction could also be violated if judge leniency impacts future outcomes through
17:688:53724:17:19:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:channels other than bankruptcy protection. For example, the exclusion restriction would be violated
17:689:53823:19:15:87:539:196:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:9To put the magnitude of the age and tenure correlations in Table 3 in context, we compare the implied bias
17:690:53930:15:11:72:540:181:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:in our reduced form earnings results reported in Section VA. Controlling only for office by month fixed effects, an
17:691:54045:11:11:72:540:170:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:OLS regression of average earnings over the first five post-filing earnings on age suggests that being a year older
17:692:54160:11:11:72:540:159:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:is associated with earnings that are $176.86 lower. Controlling for all of the covariates listed in Table 3, being a
17:693:54276:11:11:72:540:148:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:year older is associated with earnings that are $252.70 lower. An additional year of job tenure is associated with
17:694:54390:11:11:72:540:137:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:earnings that are $1,917.81 higher when controlling only for office by month fixed effects, and $1,265.64 higher when
17:695:54507:11:11:72:540:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:controlling for all other covariates in Table 3. Thus, a one standard deviation (three percentage point) increase in
17:696:54623:11:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:judge leniency is associated with a -$0.000037 to $0.000037 change in earnings due to the differences in age observed
17:697:54740:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:in Table 3, and a $0.002885 to $0.004430 change in earnings due to the differences in job tenure observed in Table 3.
17:698:54857:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:In contrast, our reduced form results plotted in Figure 3 show that a one percentage point increase in judge leniency
17:699:54974:11:11:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:is associated with a $128.55 increase in post-filing earnings. Results are similar for employment, mortality, and home
17:700:55092:11:0:72:117:71:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:foreclosure.
18:701:55106:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:if more lenient judges are also more likely to provide financial counseling to debtors, and that
18:702:55202:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:financial counseling has an independent impact on future outcomes.  If judge leniency impacts
18:703:55295:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:future outcomes through any other channels, then the resulting local average treatment effect would
18:704:55394:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:incorporate any additional impacts associated with judge assignment. The assumption that judges
18:705:55489:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:only systematically affect debtor outcomes through bankruptcy is fundamentally untestable, and
18:706:55583:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:our estimates should be interpreted with this potential caveat in mind. However, we argue that this
18:707:55682:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:exclusion assumption is reasonable in our setting. Recall that bankruptcy judges typically interact
18:708:55781:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with debtors only at the confirmation hearing, while the separately assigned court trustee handles
18:709:55879:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:all pre- and post-filing issues. Thus, it seems unlikely that judges would confer significant benefits
18:710:55981:16:17:72:394:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to debtors other than through their ruling on the bankruptcy filing.
18:711:56049:17:16:88:539:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our third identifying assumption is that there is a monotonic impact of judge assignment on the
18:712:56144:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:probability of receiving bankruptcy protection. The monotonicity assumption implies that being
18:713:56238:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:assigned to a more (less) lenient judge does not result in a decrease (increase) in the likelihood of
18:714:56339:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:receiving bankruptcy protection. This monotonicity assumption would be violated if judges differ
18:715:56435:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the types of filings they treat more leniently. For example, the monotonicity assumption would
18:716:56532:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:be invalid if some judges treat women more leniently, while other judges do not treat women more
18:717:56628:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:leniently. If the monotonicity assumption is violated, our estimates from equation (8) would still be
18:718:56729:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a weighted average of marginal treatment effects, but the weights would not sum to one (Angrist,
18:719:56825:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Imbens, and Rubin 1996, Heckman and Vytlacil 2005). The monotonicity assumption is therefore
18:720:56917:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:necessary to interpret our estimates as a well defined local average treatment effect. The bias away
18:721:57017:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:from this local average treatment effect is an increasing function of the number of individuals for
18:722:57116:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whom the monotonicity assumption does not hold and the difference in the marginal treatment
18:723:57207:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effects for those individuals for whom the monotonicity assumption does and does not hold. The
18:724:57301:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:amount of bias is also a decreasing function of the first stage relationship described by equation (9)
18:725:57403:17:16:72:249:314:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f4:(Angrist, Imbens, and Rubin 1996).10
18:726:57439:16:17:88:539:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:To partially test the monotonicity assumption, Appendix Figure 5 plots judge leniency measures
18:727:57533:17:16:71:539:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that are calculated separately for each judge by gender, race, baseline income, age, and home
18:728:57626:16:17:71:539:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ownership. We also report the coefficient and standard error from an OLS regression relating each
18:729:57723:17:16:71:539:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:measure of judge leniency. Consistent with our monotonicity assumption, judges exhibit remarkably
18:730:57820:16:17:71:539:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:similar tendencies across observably different filers. Regressing the judge leniency for male filers on
18:731:57923:17:16:71:539:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:those for female filers yields a point estimate of 0.838. For white and non-white filers, the point
18:732:58022:16:16:71:539:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimate is 1.005, for high and low baseline earnings the coefficient is 0.998, for filers older and
18:733:58122:16:17:71:539:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:younger than 40 the coefficient is 1.104, and for those matched to a home and those not matched
18:734:58217:17:16:71:539:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to a home the coefficient is 0.889. None of the results suggest that the monotonicity assumption is
18:735:58316:16:53:71:173:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:invalid in our setting.
18:736:58339:53:15:83:539:97:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:10Small and Tan (2007), Klein (2010), de Chaisemartin (2014), and Huber and Mellace (2011) establish conditions
18:737:58450:15:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:under which it is possible to interpret the instrumental variables estimates as a LATE for a different population when
18:738:58568:10:0:72:236:72:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:the monotonicity assumption is violated.
19:739:58610:0:17:95:516:708:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:V. The Impact of Chapter 13 Bankruptcy Protection on Labor Supply,
19:740:58676:17:22:218:413:691:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:Mortality, and Home Foreclosure
19:741:58707:22:23:265:346:669:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A. Labor Supply
19:742:58722:23:17:72:540:646:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:As a benchmark for evaluating the causal effects described below, we begin with a descriptive
19:743:58815:17:16:72:540:629:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:analysis of granted and dismissed filers. Figure 2 plots average pre- and post-filing earnings and
19:744:58913:16:16:72:540:613:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:employment for our estimation sample. Earnings include both wage and self-employment earnings
19:745:59006:16:17:72:540:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:including zeros.11To aid in the interpretation of the results, we plot expected outcomes calculated
19:746:59105:17:16:72:540:580:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:using a regression of the outcome five years before filing on controls for gender, race, a quadratic
19:747:59205:16:17:72:540:564:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in age, a quadratic in tenure, industry fixed effects, and earnings in the previous five years. We
19:748:59303:17:16:72:540:547:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:then predict the outcome for the four years before filing and the five years after filing using age and
19:749:59406:16:17:72:160:531:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tenure coefficients.
19:750:59426:17:16:88:539:514:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Filers granted Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection earn $5,000 to $5,500 more than dismissed
19:751:59515:16:16:72:540:498:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers in the years leading up to filing.  Earnings for both groups fall two to three years before
19:752:59613:16:17:72:539:482:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filing, with a larger dip for dismissed filers.12The post-filing earnings of dismissed filers dip further,
19:753:59719:17:16:72:540:465:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:falling about $4,000 below the expected trajectory five years after filing. In contrast to the large
19:754:59819:16:17:72:540:449:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and permanent decline in earnings experienced by dismissed filers, individuals granted bankruptcy
19:755:59916:17:16:72:540:432:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection appear to have no long-term earnings losses. These descriptive trends suggest that any
19:756:60013:16:17:72:540:416:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:causal impacts of bankruptcy protection are likely to be driven by the deterioration of outcomes
19:757:60109:17:16:72:540:399:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:among dismissed filers, as opposed to gains by granted filers.  This interpretation suggests that
19:758:60206:16:17:72:540:383:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy protection mitigates the long-term consequences of financial shocks that might otherwise
19:759:60305:17:16:72:464:366:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:harm debtors, but does not confer any benefits in the absence of a financial shock.
19:760:60388:16:16:88:539:350:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Reduced form estimates of the impact of judge leniency on average earnings and employment
19:761:60477:16:17:72:540:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:over the first five post-filing years are presented in Figure 3. Following our first stage results from
19:762:60580:17:16:72:540:317:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Figure 1, we construct each plot by regressing each outcome on office by month-of-filing fixed effects,
19:763:60683:16:17:72:540:301:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:calculating residuals, and then adding the mean outcome to each residual to facilitate interpretation
19:764:60784:17:16:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the scale. The solid line and corresponding coefficient show the best linear fit estimated on the
19:765:60884:16:17:72:540:268:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:underlying micro data controlling for office by month-of-filing fixed effects, with standard errors
19:766:60983:17:16:72:202:251:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:clustered at the office level.
19:767:61013:16:16:88:539:235:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Figure 3 shows that being assigned to a more lenient judge significantly increases post-filing
19:768:61107:16:17:72:540:219:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:earnings and employment.  A one standard deviation (three percentage point) increase in judge
19:769:61200:17:28:72:540:202:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:leniency increases post-filing earnings by $128.55 relative to the baseline mean of $22,115. Employ-
19:770:61300:28:15:83:539:174:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:11Appendix Table 4 displays the same information in tabular form. Appendix Figure 6 plots mean and median
19:771:61405:15:11:72:540:159:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:earnings with and without zeros included.  Median earnings are lower than mean earnings for both granted and
19:772:61513:11:11:72:540:148:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:dismissed filers, but the same qualitative trends exist before and after filing as in Figure 2.  Mean and median
19:773:61625:11:11:72:540:137:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:earnings without zeros included also follow the same trend as Figure 2.  Two-stage least squares estimates that
19:774:61736:11:7:72:485:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:condition on non-zero earnings are somewhat larger than those reported here (See Appendix Table 5).
19:775:61835:7:15:83:539:119:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:12The fall in pre-filing earnings is likely related to the “Ashenfelter dip” – the drop in earnings among participants
19:776:61953:15:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:in job training programs – discussed by Ashenfelter (1978), Ashenfelter and Card (1985), and Heckman and Hotz
19:777:62062:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:(1989).  In our context, the negative earnings shocks before bankruptcy filing may result in OLS estimates with
19:778:62173:11:11:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:a non-filing control group to overstate the true gains of bankruptcy if there is mean reversion in earnings, and to
19:779:62288:11:0:72:433:71:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:understate the impact of bankruptcy if shocks have consequences that increase over time.
20:780:62378:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ment over the same time period increases by 0.2 percentage points relative to the baseline mean of
20:781:62476:17:16:72:133:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:81.3 percent.
20:782:62489:16:17:88:539:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Figure 4 presents corresponding two-stage least squares results measuring the causal impact of
20:783:62583:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection on earnings and employment. We use judge leniencyZijctas an
20:784:62675:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:instrumental variable for bankruptcy protection, and control for gender, race, five-year age effects,
20:785:62776:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a five-year average of baseline employment, a five-year average of baseline earnings, and office by
20:786:62875:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:month-of-filing fixed effects. For treatment effects in the baseline period, we control for gender, race,
20:787:62980:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:five-year age effects, office by month-of-filing fixed effects, and average employment and earnings in
20:788:63082:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the years prior to the baseline year under consideration. Standard errors are clustered at the office
20:789:63183:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:level throughout. We estimate the impact of bankruptcy protection for each year separately. Table
20:790:63280:17:16:72:428:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:4 presents estimates pooling outcomes across the first five post-filing years.
20:791:63358:16:17:88:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There is a large and precisely estimated impact of Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection on post-
20:792:63450:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filing earnings and employment. In the first full year after filing, the marginal recipient of Chapter 13
20:793:63555:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection earns $6,228 more than the marginal dismissed filer. The impact of Chapter 13 protection
20:794:63654:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:remains both economically and statistically significant for the first five post-filing years. Pooling
20:795:63755:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:outcomes across those five years, the marginal recipient of Chapter 13 earns $5,562 more than the
20:796:63852:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:marginal dismissed filer, a 25.1 percent increase from the baseline mean. The earnings estimates
20:797:63948:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:reported in Table 4 are similar to those suggested by the descriptive trends in Figure 2, and formal
20:798:64048:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:event study estimates presented in Section VE. Conversely, our two-stage least squares estimates
20:799:64144:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are considerably larger than cross-sectional (e.g.  Han and Li 2007, 2011) and within-individual
20:800:64240:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimates (e.g. Cohen-Cole, Duygan-Bump and Montoriol-Garriga 2009) that do not use dismissed
20:801:64333:17:16:72:208:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers as a comparison group.
20:802:64362:16:16:88:539:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Over the first five post-filing years, Chapter 13 also increases employment by 6.8 percentage
20:803:64455:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:points, a 8.3 percent increase from the baseline mean. This point estimate suggests that approx-
20:804:64551:17:16:72:539:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:imately($22,115·6.8) = $1,503, or 27 percent, of the earnings estimate can be explained by a
20:805:64643:16:17:72:232:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:decline in labor force attachment.
20:806:64677:17:16:88:539:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our two-stage least squares estimates can only be interpreted as the causal effect of bankruptcy
20:807:64773:16:17:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection if judge leniency is not systematically related to unobserved filer characteristics. One way
20:808:64876:17:16:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to evaluate the validity of this assumption is to a estimate the impact of bankruptcy protection in
20:809:64975:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the years before a debtor files. Consistent with our identifying assumptions discussed above, there
20:810:65074:17:16:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is no systematic relationship between bankruptcy protection and either earnings or employment in
20:811:65170:16:16:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the pre-filing years, with the estimated coefficients being economically and statistically insignificant.
20:812:65275:16:17:88:539:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Appendix Table 2 presents estimates using a variety of specifications and instruments to assess
20:813:65370:17:16:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the robustness of our main results. Column 2 replicates our preferred estimates from Table 4 using
20:814:65468:16:17:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:leave-one-out judge leniency as an instrument for Chapter 13 protection. Column 3 uses a leave-
20:815:65563:17:16:72:540:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:month-out measure of judge leniency – where we calculate judge leniency only using cases in the
20:816:65658:16:17:72:540:117:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:11 other months of the filing year – as an instrument for Chapter 13 protection. Measuring judge
20:817:65754:17:16:72:540:100:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:leniency only using cases from the other 11 months purges any remaining correlation between a
20:818:65847:16:0:72:540:84:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filer’s outcomes and our instrument introduced by the estimation of the office by month-of-filing
21:819:65946:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:fixed effects in our first and second stage regressions. Column 4 uses a leave-one-out measure of judge
21:820:66049:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:leniency measured over the first 90 post-filing days as an instrument. Column 5 uses a randomly
21:821:66144:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:selected subset of 50 percent of filers to calculate a leave-month-out measure of judge leniency that is
21:822:66248:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:used as an instrument in the mutually exclusive subset of filers. Columns 6 through 8 present results
21:823:66349:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that use judge fixed effects as instruments for bankruptcy protection estimated using two-stage least
21:824:66450:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:squares, LIML, and jackknife IV, respectively. All regressions control for gender, race, five-year age
21:825:66552:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effects, a five-year average of baseline employment, a five-year average of baseline earnings, and
21:826:66650:17:16:72:481:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:office by month-of-filing fixed effects, with standard errors clustered at the office level.
21:827:66742:16:16:88:539:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our two-stage least squares estimates are robust to the choice of instrument and estimation
21:828:66833:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:method. The impact of Chapter 13 protection on post-filing earnings is $5,602 in the leave-month-
21:829:66930:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:out specification, $9,126 in the 90-day judge leniency specification, $4,628 in the split sample spec-
21:830:67032:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ification, $4,445 in the two-stage least squares judge fixed effects specification, $4,263 in the LIML
21:831:67134:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:specification, and $4,463 in the jackknife IV specification.  Due to the relatively large standard
21:832:67232:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:errors when using judge fixed effects as instruments, we cannot reject the hypothesis that the es-
21:833:67330:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:timated treatment effects are identical to our preferred estimate of $5,562 for all of our estimates
21:834:67430:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:except the 90-day judge leniency specification. The results follow a similar pattern for employment,
21:835:67530:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:while the mortality and foreclosure results are larger when using judge fixed effects. None of the
21:836:67628:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:point estimates for employment, mortality, and foreclosure are statistically distinguishable from our
21:837:67729:16:17:72:276:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:preferred estimates in column 2 of Table 4.
21:838:67772:17:16:88:539:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Appendix Table 6 presents two-stage least squares results using our preferred specification for
21:839:67867:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the sixth through tenth post-filing years. We restrict the sample to filings originating between 1992
21:840:67968:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and 2000. Filings originating after 2000 are excluded because we do not observe post-filing outcomes
21:841:68068:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for all ten years for these individuals. In this sample of older filings, Chapter 13 protection increases
21:842:68173:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the marginal recipient’s annual earnings by $6,772 in the sixth through tenth post-filing years. These
21:843:68275:17:16:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:results suggest that the impact of bankruptcy protection is persistent after the completion of the
21:844:68373:16:17:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:repayment plan. The probability of being employed is also 6.6 percentage points higher in the sixth
21:845:68472:17:16:72:220:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:through tenth post-filing years.
21:846:68504:16:17:88:539:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 5 presents two-stage least squares results from our preferred specification separately by
21:847:68599:17:16:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filer gender, race, age, baseline earnings, and being matched to a home. The effects of Chapter 13
21:848:68697:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection on annual earnings are somewhat larger for female and non-white filers, though neither
21:849:68794:17:16:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:difference is statistically significant. There are significantly larger impacts of Chapter 13 protec-
21:850:68895:16:16:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tion on younger filers, likely because older filers in our sample have already left the labor market.
21:851:68996:16:17:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Specifically, Chapter 13 increases the annual earnings of filers who are 25 to 40 years old by $7,833
21:852:69097:17:16:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and the annual earnings of filers who are 40 and 60 years old by $6,299, while having no discernible
21:853:69197:16:17:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effect on filers who are 60 or older at the time of filing. Chapter 13 protection also has a larger
21:854:69296:17:16:72:540:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:impact on filers with above median earnings. Chapter 13 increases annual earnings by $8,650 for
21:855:69391:16:17:72:540:117:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers with above median earnings, compared to an increase of $1,691 for filers with below median
21:856:69488:17:16:72:540:100:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:earnings. The impact of Chapter 13 protection on employment is also 6.0 percentage points higher
21:857:69584:16:0:72:540:84:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for filers with above median baseline earnings. This may be the result of higher earning filers facing
22:858:69688:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a higher marginal rate of garnishment, or non-linearities in the elasticity of labor supply. In Section
22:859:69791:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:VD, we show that the garnishment channel is at least partially responsible for the pattern of results
22:860:69892:16:17:72:168:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:observed in Table 5.
22:861:69912:17:16:88:539:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel D of Table 4 presents results for additional labor supply outcomes available in the SSA
22:862:70005:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:data. We estimate the impact of Chapter 13 protection on the average of each outcome over the
22:863:70098:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:first five post-filing years. Among eligible filers, bankruptcy protection decreases the receipt of SSI
22:864:70201:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by 12.8 percentage points, though the point estimate is only significant at the ten percent level.
22:865:70299:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Bankruptcy protection also appears to have little impact on the receipt of DI or on annual 401k
22:866:70394:16:32:72:137:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:contributions.
22:867:70408:32:23:275:336:545:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B. Mortality
22:868:70420:23:17:72:540:522:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The reduced form estimate of judge leniency on five-year mortality is presented in Figure 3, and the
22:869:70520:17:16:72:540:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:corresponding two-stage least squares estimates are presented in Figure 4. The dependent variable
22:870:70617:16:16:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for each regression is an indicator for being deceased in or before the specified year. Trends in the
22:871:70718:16:17:72:239:473:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:raw data are presented in Figure 2.
22:872:70753:17:16:88:539:456:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In the first full year after filing, only 0.3 percent of filers granted Chapter 13 protection are
22:873:70850:16:17:72:540:440:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:deceased, compared to 1.15 percent of dismissed filers. Five years after filing, 2.1 percent of filers
22:874:70952:17:16:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:granted Chapter 13 protection are deceased, compared to 4.0 percent of dismissed filers.  These
22:875:71047:16:17:72:540:407:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:statistics suggest that dismissed bankruptcy filers have extremely high mortality rates. The annual
22:876:71146:17:16:72:540:390:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mortality rate for individuals age 25-70 in the United States is about 0.45 percent, one-third to
22:877:71243:16:16:72:540:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:two-fifths the mortality risk of dismissed filers. The annual mortality rate for a national population
22:878:71345:16:17:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with a similar age profile as our estimation sample is 0.3 percent, one-quarter to one-third the
22:879:71441:17:16:72:539:341:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mortality risk of dismissed filers (CDC 2014).13The high mortality rates among dismissed filers
22:880:71536:16:17:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are consistent with the high rates of medical debt (Domowitz and Sartain 1999, Sullivan, Warren,
22:881:71632:17:16:72:540:308:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Westbrook 2000, Warren, Sullivan, and Jacoby 2000, Himmelstein et al. 2009) and high levels
22:882:71727:16:17:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of self-reported stress (Porter 2011) among bankruptcy filers. The mortality rates among dismissed
22:883:71825:17:16:72:540:275:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers are also consistent with the high mortality rates reported among displaced workers. Sullivan
22:884:71924:16:17:72:540:259:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and von Watcher (2009) find average annual mortality rates of 0.52 percent among displaced workers
22:885:72022:17:16:72:540:242:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:age 28-57, nearly 30 percent higher than the national mortality rate for similarly aged individuals
22:886:72121:16:16:72:210:226:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:during the same time period.
22:887:72149:16:17:88:539:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Turning to our causal estimates, the reduced form results from Figure 4 show that being assigned
22:888:72245:17:16:72:540:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to a more lenient judge decreases five-year mortality. A one standard deviation increase in judge
22:889:72342:16:17:72:540:177:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:leniency decreases five-year mortality by 0.0003 percentage points relative to the dismissed filer
22:890:72440:17:30:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mean of 4.0 percentage points.  Note that we use the dismissed filer mean as a reference point
22:891:72534:30:15:83:539:130:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:13The CDC reports the annual population, number of deaths, and mortality rates for five year age groups. We
22:892:72641:15:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:calculate the annual mortality rate in 2011 for the 25 to 39 age group by dividing the number of deaths by the total
22:893:72757:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:population of people in the combined 25 to 29, 30 to 34, and 35 to 39 age groups. A similar approach is used to
22:894:72868:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:calculate the mortality rates for the 40 to 59 and 60 to 70 age groups, using the appropriate age groups from the
22:895:72981:11:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:CDC. We adjust for the age profile of our sample by calculating a weighted average of mortality rates where weights
22:896:73096:10:0:72:340:72:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:are proportionate to the size of the each age cohort in our sample.
23:897:73165:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:because the deceased cannot file for bankruptcy protection, making the baseline mortality rate zero
23:898:73264:17:16:72:149:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by construction.
23:899:73280:16:17:88:539:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In the two-stage least squares results, Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection lowers five-year mor-
23:900:73374:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tality by a statistically significant 1.2 percentage points, a 30.0 percent decrease from the control
23:901:73475:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mean. Aggregating the mortality effects across the first five post-filing years, our results imply that
23:902:73578:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the marginal recipient of Chapter 13 protection is alive for 0.053 more years than the marginal
23:903:73673:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:non-recipient. In a sample of debtors filing between 1992 and 2000, Chapter 13 decreases ten-year
23:904:73770:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mortality by 1.5 percentage points, though the estimate is not statistically significant. We wish to
23:905:73870:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:emphasize that due to the relative imprecision of our mortality estimates, the 95 percent confidence
23:906:73970:16:17:72:412:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:intervals include both very small and implausibly large point estimates.
23:907:74042:17:16:88:539:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel B of Table 5 reports two-stage least squares results interacted by filer gender, race, age,
23:908:74139:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:baseline earnings, and being matched to a home. The effect of Chapter 13 protection on mortality
23:909:74235:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is larger for filers who are white, have above median baseline earnings, and are not matched to a
23:910:74332:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:home at baseline. However, the most striking pattern is by age. Chapter 13 protection decreases
23:911:74427:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:five-year mortality by 10.9 percentage points for filers 60 and older at the time of filing, despite
23:912:74527:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:having little to no impact on earnings for these filers. In contrast, Chapter 13 decreases five-year
23:913:74627:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mortality by only 2.2 percentage points for filers between 25 and 40, and 1.7 percentage points for
23:914:74726:17:32:72:189:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers between 40 and 60.
23:915:74751:32:23:253:354:397:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:C. Home Foreclosure
23:916:74770:23:16:72:540:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The reduced form estimate of judge leniency on five-year foreclosure is presented in Figure 3, and
23:917:74868:16:17:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the corresponding two-stage least squares estimates are presented in Figure 4. The sample includes
23:918:74966:17:16:72:540:341:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filings in our estimation sample in county by year bins covered by the DataQuick records. Home
23:919:75060:16:17:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:foreclosure is an indicator for a filer’s home receiving a notice of default, receiving a notice of transfer
23:920:75168:17:16:72:540:308:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:or sale, or having been transferred to a REO or a guarantor on or before the indicated year. Note
23:921:75265:16:17:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that we are unable to estimate the impact of bankruptcy protection on pre-filing foreclosure as we
23:922:75363:17:16:72:540:275:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:only have address information for the year of filing, and were unable to match pre-filing transactions
23:923:75465:16:17:72:350:259:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to filers. Trends in the raw data are presented in Figure 2.
23:924:75525:17:16:88:539:242:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection significantly lowers the probability of home foreclosure. In
23:925:75618:16:16:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the raw data plotted in Figure 2, five-year foreclosure rates are less than 2.5 percent for filers
23:926:75716:16:17:72:540:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:receiving bankruptcy protection, compared to 14.9 percent for dismissed filers. This implies that
23:927:75813:17:16:72:540:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:approximately one-third of dismissed filers matched to a home experience a home foreclosure within
23:928:75911:16:17:72:540:177:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the first five post-filing years. Note that we use the dismissed filer mean for reference, as we only
23:929:76012:17:16:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:observe a filer’s address at the time of filing. Because the vast majority of foreclosures result in a
23:930:76114:16:17:72:521:144:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:change of address, we are largely unable to measure the probability of foreclosure before filing.
23:931:76211:17:16:88:539:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our reduced form results from Figure 3 show that being assigned to a more lenient judge has an
23:932:76305:16:16:72:540:111:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:economically and statistically significant effect on post-filing foreclosure. A one standard deviation
23:933:76407:16:17:72:540:95:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:increase in judge leniency decreases five-year foreclosure by 0.00459 percentage points relative to the
23:934:76510:17:0:72:540:78:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:dismissed filer mean of 14.9 percentage points. In the two-stage least squares estimates, Chapter 13
24:935:76612:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection decreases foreclosure by 11.9 percentage points in the first full post-filing year and 16.7
24:936:76714:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:percentage points in the second post-filing year. Foreclosure rates are 19.1 percentage points lower
24:937:76814:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:five years after filing, a 127.5 percent decrease from the dismissed filer mean. Conditional on being
24:938:76915:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:matched to a home, Chapter 13 protection decreases five-year home foreclosure by 35.3 percentage
24:939:77011:16:17:72:104:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:points.
24:940:77018:17:16:88:539:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In Appendix Table 5, we show that bankruptcy protection also significantly decreases voluntary
24:941:77112:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and short home sales.  Distress sales, which include both foreclosures and short sales, are 22.2
24:942:77208:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:percentage points lower after five years. Home sales, which include all types of housing transactions,
24:943:77310:16:16:72:301:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are 33.9 percentage points lower after five years.
24:944:77360:16:17:88:539:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel C of Table 5 reports subsample results. The effect of Chapter 13 protection on foreclosure
24:945:77456:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is larger for filers with low baseline earnings and filers who are 60 or older at the time of filing.
24:946:77557:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:These results may be due to these filers being more at risk of foreclosure or having fewer alternatives
24:947:77660:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:if a bankruptcy filing is dismissed. However, the precise mechanisms for this pattern of results are
24:948:77760:16:32:72:109:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:unclear.
24:949:77768:32:23:215:396:463:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:D. Discussion and Potential Channels
24:950:77804:23:17:72:540:440:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Why are there such large benefits of receiving bankruptcy protection?  In this section, we first
24:951:77900:17:16:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:explore whether protection from wage garnishment and reduced economic instability can explain
24:952:77993:16:17:72:540:407:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:our labor supply results. We then conclude by considering potential explanations for our mortality
24:953:78091:17:16:72:102:390:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:result.
24:954:78098:16:16:88:539:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:One explanation for our results is that Chapter 13 maintains the incentive to work by protecting
24:955:78194:16:17:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:future earnings from wage garnishment. In this scenario, dismissed filers reduce their labor supply
24:956:78293:17:16:72:540:341:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:due to the tax on earnings imposed by wage garnishment. Table 6 partially tests this hypothesis
24:957:78388:16:17:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by estimating the impact of Chapter 13 protection interacted with proxies of garnishment risk.
24:958:78482:17:16:72:540:308:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Columns 1 and 2 of Table 6 present results for filers in the four states that prohibit wage garnishment
24:959:78585:16:17:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:– Florida, Pennsylvania, South Carolina, and Texas – and filers in states that allow at least some
24:960:78683:17:16:72:540:275:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:wage garnishment. The impact of Chapter 13 on annual earnings over the first five post-filing years
24:961:78782:16:17:72:540:259:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is $5,635 in states that allow garnishment, compared to $3,193 in the four states that prohibit
24:962:78877:17:16:72:540:242:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:garnishment. The pattern of results is reversed for employment, however, with larger impacts in
24:963:78972:16:16:72:518:226:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the four states that prohibit garnishment, though the difference is not statistically significant.
24:964:79070:16:17:88:539:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Columns 3 through 7 exploit both within- and across-state variation in garnishment laws to
24:965:79160:17:16:72:540:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimate results for filers who are likely to be subject to different marginal garnishment rates.
24:966:79257:16:17:72:540:177:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Within each state, wage garnishments are a non-linear function of earnings. For example, in states
24:967:79355:17:16:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that follow the federal guidelines, creditors are allowed to garnish each additional dollar of disposable
24:968:79460:16:17:72:540:144:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:earnings between 30 and 40 times the minimum wage, but only 25 cents of every additional dollar
24:969:79555:17:16:72:540:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:after that point. There is also across-state variation in garnishment rates. Twelve states have lower
24:970:79656:16:16:72:540:111:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:marginal garnishment rates, ten have lower caps on the total amount that can be garnished, and
24:971:79750:16:17:72:540:95:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:four states prohibit wage garnishment altogether. In each of these states, the more stringent state
24:972:79849:17:0:72:332:78:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:regulation takes precedence over the federal guidelines.
25:973:79907:0:17:88:539:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We exploit this variation in garnishment laws by estimating the impact of bankruptcy interacted
25:974:80002:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with the marginal garnishment rate a filer is likely to face under both state and federal law.14Our
25:975:80101:16:30:72:180:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimating equation is:
25:976:80124:30:30:88:539:646:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:yit=α+αot+βXi+γ00BiG00+γ2525BiG2525+γ100100BiG100100+γ250BiG250+γ1000BiG1000+εit(11)
25:977:80208:30:16:71:540:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereGyxis an indicator for a filer facing a marginal garnishment rate ofxin his or her state of
25:978:80304:16:17:71:540:600:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filing and a marginal garnishment ofyunder federal law. We instrument for eachBiGyxusing the
25:979:80396:17:16:71:540:583:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:interaction between judge leniency and the garnishment binZijctGyx. We estimate the impact of
25:980:80489:16:17:71:539:567:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy separately for filers facing different state and federal garnishment rates to control for
25:981:80589:17:16:71:539:550:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:any differential effects of bankruptcy correlated with baseline earnings that are unrelated to the
25:982:80687:16:16:71:539:534:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:marginal garnishment rate.  For example,γ250measures the impact of Chapter 13 protection on
25:983:80778:16:17:71:539:518:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers with higher earnings who are exempt from garnishment in their state of filing, but who would
25:984:80877:17:16:71:539:501:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:have been subject to 25 percent garnishment under federal law, whileγ2525measures the impact of
25:985:80972:16:17:71:539:485:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 13 on filers with higher earnings in states that do not exempt them from garnishment.
25:986:81065:17:16:71:539:468:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Thus,γ250measures the effect of bankruptcy without garnishment protections for higher-earning
25:987:81158:16:17:71:539:452:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers, whileγ2525measures the effect of Chapter 13 with garnishment protections for higher-earning
25:988:81257:17:16:71:96:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers.
25:989:81264:16:16:88:539:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The effect of Chapter 13 protection is small and imprecisely estimated for filers unlikely to
25:990:81357:16:17:71:539:403:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:face wage garnishment. The impact on annual earnings is negative $471 for filers subject to no
25:991:81451:17:16:71:539:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:garnishment under both state and federal law, $5,607 for filers who would have been subject to
25:992:81545:16:17:71:539:370:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:marginal garnishment of 25 percent had they lived in another state, and negative $1,759 for filers
25:993:81643:17:16:71:539:353:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:who would have been subject to marginal garnishment of 100 percent had they lived in another
25:994:81735:16:17:71:469:337:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:state. None of the point estimates are statistically significant at conventional levels.
25:995:81823:17:16:88:539:320:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In contrast, there is a large and precisely estimated impact of Chapter 13 on filers subject to
25:996:81918:16:16:71:539:304:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the 25 percent marginal garnishment rate in their state of filing. The impact on annual earnings
25:997:82014:16:17:71:539:288:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is $7,892 for filers subject to marginal garnishment of 25 percent under both state and federal law.
25:998:82114:17:16:71:539:271:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Due to the imprecision of the point estimates, the estimate is not statistically different than that
25:999:82214:16:17:71:539:255:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for filers subject to no garnishment under state law but 25 percent under federal law (p-value =
25:1000:82310:17:16:71:539:238:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:0.572). For filers subject to the 100 percent marginal garnishment rate, the impact is a statistically
25:1001:82412:16:17:71:539:222:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:insignificant $7,435. The difference between this estimate and the estimate for filers subject to no
25:1002:82512:17:16:71:539:205:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:garnishment under state law but 100 percent under federal law is marginally significant (p-value
25:1003:82608:16:17:71:539:189:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:= 0.10).  However, if we take these estimates from columns 4 and 6 at face value, the implied
25:1004:82701:17:20:71:539:172:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:elasticity of earnings with respect to garnishment is about 0.94 for the 25 percent bracket.15All of
25:1005:82801:20:15:83:539:152:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:14We estimate disposable earnings using pre-tax earnings in the five most recent pre-filing years and the tax rate
25:1006:82915:15:11:72:540:137:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:implied by the NBER TAXSIM federal and state income tax calculator. We assume that all filers are the only earner
25:1007:83028:11:7:72:428:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:in their households, as we do not observe marital status in the bankruptcy or SSA data.
25:1008:83115:7:15:83:539:119:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:15The earnings elasticity with respect to garnishment is equal to the log change in taxable earnings divided by the
25:1009:83230:15:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:log change in the net tax rate. We assume that the state and federal earnings tax rate is 20 percent, implying that
25:1010:83345:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:the net tax and garnishment rate is1−(1−0.2)(1−0.25) = 40percent. Finally, we use the impact of bankruptcy
25:1011:83451:11:11:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:on filers facing no garnishment in their state of filing who would have faced a 25 percent garnishment under federal
25:1012:83567:11:0:72:540:71:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:law as a counterfactual impact. These assumptions imply an elasticity of earnings with respect to garnishment of
26:1013:83681:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the results from Table 6 are broadly consistent with bankruptcy protection increasing the incentive
26:1014:83780:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to work by lowering the effective marginal tax rate on earnings. Nevertheless, it is unlikely that
26:1015:83878:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a lower marginal tax rate explains all of our results. Previous studies suggest that the intensive
26:1016:83976:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:marginal elasticity of earnings with respect to the net-of-tax rate is approximately 0.25 (e.g. Chetty
26:1017:84078:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2012), implying that a 25 percent marginal tax cut should increase earnings by about 6.25 percent,
26:1018:84176:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:24.9 percent of our earnings estimate from Table 4. Our implied elasticity measure is likely to be
26:1019:84274:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:positively biased by other laws and regulations correlated with wage garnishment policies, such as
26:1020:84372:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:restrictions on third-party debt collectors. We also note that the standard errors in Table 6 are
26:1021:84469:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:large enough that the implied elasticity with respect to earnings includes a wide range of estimates.
26:1022:84570:16:17:88:539:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A second explanation for the estimated effects is that bankruptcy protection maintains economic
26:1023:84665:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:stability. Bankruptcy protection discharges most debts, allows debtors to repay mortgage arrears,
26:1024:84762:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and puts a hold on almost all debt collection efforts. These features of the bankruptcy code may
26:1025:84858:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:maintain economic stability by allowing debtors to avoid eviction or home foreclosure, reducing the
26:1026:84957:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:incentive to strategically move across state lines or change jobs to avoid creditors, or preventing
26:1027:85056:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:sharp drops in consumption that have important long-term consequences. Consistent with this ex-
26:1028:85151:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:planation, our earnings result is of similar magnitude (in the opposite direction) to the estimated
26:1029:85250:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effect of job loss (e.g. von Wachter, Song, and Machester 2009), suggesting that bankruptcy pro-
26:1030:85346:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tection may be able to offset the adverse consequences of a financial shock such as job loss. This
26:1031:85444:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:interpretation is also consistent with our results from Figure 2, which show a significant deterioration
26:1032:85548:17:16:72:503:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of outcomes among dismissed filers, but few gains for filers granted bankruptcy protection.
26:1033:85639:16:17:88:539:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We present further evidence on this issue by examining filer mobility as proxied by firm EIN.
26:1034:85732:17:16:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 7 presents estimates of the impact of Chapter 13 protection on the probability of working
26:1035:85827:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the same baseline job, industry, county, and state. We also present results for job tenure and
26:1036:85924:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:average firm wages. The sample is restricted to filers with at least one year of employment in both
26:1037:86023:17:16:72:218:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the pre- and post-filing period.
26:1038:86055:16:17:88:539:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Bankruptcy protection increases the probability of working in the same (2-digit NAICS) indus-
26:1039:86148:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:try by 23.8 percentage points, a 42.7 percent change from the baseline mean of 55.7 percent, and
26:1040:86244:16:17:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:increases the probability that a filer stays at his or her baseline job by 24.6 percentage points, a 49.0
26:1041:86349:17:16:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:percent change from the baseline mean of 50.2 percent. There is also a large impact of bankruptcy
26:1042:86446:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection on geographic mobility, with bankruptcy protection increasing the probability that a filer
26:1043:86547:17:16:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:works in his or her baseline county by 22.9 percentage points, a 39.7 percent increase, and his or her
26:1044:86649:16:16:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:baseline state by 15.3 percentage points, a 24.4 percent increase. Job tenure and average firm wages
26:1045:86749:16:17:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are also higher, suggesting that this increase in economic stability is beneficial for the worker. In
26:1046:86850:17:16:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Appendix Table 7, we find some evidence that the mobility estimates are larger in states that allow
26:1047:86949:16:17:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:garnishment, though not all of the differences are statistically significant. The estimated impacts
26:1048:87048:17:16:72:540:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:also tend to increase with the marginal garnishment bracket, though the differences are not statis-
26:1049:87147:16:29:72:540:117:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tically significant and the estimated effects remain relatively large in the no garnishment bracket.
26:1050:87247:29:7:75:146:88:6:g_d0_f18:6:g_d0_f21:log(0.248)−log(0.189)
26:1051:87268:7:9:73:540:81:6:g_d0_f18:9:g_d0_f6:log(1−0.2)−log(1−0.4)= 0.94for the 25 percent bracket. Note that we are unable to calculate the elasticity for the 100
26:1052:87386:9:0:72:229:72:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:percent bracket, aslog(0)is undefined.
27:1053:87426:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Taken together with the foreclosure results, we interpret this pattern of results as suggesting that
27:1054:87526:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 13 protection maintains economic stability both by reducing forced moves from evictions
27:1055:87621:16:17:72:382:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and foreclosures and unforced, strategic moves to avoid creditors.
27:1056:87687:17:16:88:539:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We conclude this section by considering potential explanations for our mortality results.  In
27:1057:87780:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a sample of Pennsylvania workers, Sullivan and von Wachter (2009) find that job displacement
27:1058:87872:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:increases five-year mortality by 1.2 percentage points. Thus, one potential interpretation of our
27:1059:87969:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimates is that bankruptcy protection can offset much of the increased mortality risk from financial
27:1060:88071:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:distress caused by events such as job loss.  To partially test the hypothesis that the change in
27:1061:88167:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mortality that we estimate is driven by a change in earnings, we follow Sullivan and von Wachter
27:1062:88263:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(2009) and compare our two-stage least squares results for five-year mortality to the effect implied by
27:1063:88366:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the cross-sectional correlation between five-year mortality and both earnings and employment in our
27:1064:88465:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimation sample. Our two-stage least squares results suggest that bankruptcy protection increases
27:1065:88564:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:annual earnings by $5,562 and employment by 6.8 percentage points. In a regression with post-
27:1066:88657:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filing earnings, employment, and no additional controls, the estimated correlation between five-year
27:1067:88757:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mortality and average annual earnings (in $1,000s) is -0.00019, and the correlation between five-
27:1068:88854:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:year mortality and average employment is -0.00996. Taken together, these results suggest that the
27:1069:88951:16:17:72:539:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f9:change in labor supply associated with Chapter 13 protection can explain a(0.068·0.00996+5.562·
27:1070:89046:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f2:0.00019)·100 = 0.17percentage point decrease in five-year mortality, or about 14.1 percent of our
27:1071:89143:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimated treatment effect of 1.2 percentage points. This result is in stark contrast to Sullivan and
27:1072:89244:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:von Wachter (2009), who find that approximately 50 to 75 percent of the impact of job displacement
27:1073:89342:16:17:72:365:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on mortality is driven by the reduction in long-term earnings.
27:1074:89404:17:16:88:539:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Further evidence that the change in earnings associated with bankruptcy protection plays little
27:1075:89499:16:16:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to no role in explaining the mortality results comes from our subsample results reported in Panel
27:1076:89596:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B of Table 5. Recall that Chapter 13 protection decreases five-year mortality by 10.9 percentage
27:1077:89692:17:16:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:points for filers 60 and older at the time of filing, despite having little to no impact on earnings for
27:1078:89796:16:17:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:these filers. In contrast, Chapter 13 decreases five-year mortality by only 2.2 percentage points for
27:1079:89897:17:16:72:452:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers between 25 and 40, and 1.7 percentage points for filers between 40 and 60.
27:1080:89978:16:17:88:539:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There are several potentially relevant channels for our mortality result that we cannot examine
27:1081:90073:17:16:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with our current data.  For example, bankruptcy protection may decrease an individual’s stress
27:1082:90167:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by reducing contact with creditors and allowing greater control over his or her financial future.
27:1083:90264:17:16:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Consistent with this idea, 84 percent of debtors report being under extreme stress before filing for
27:1084:90364:16:16:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy, while only 35 percent report being under extreme stress after filing for bankruptcy
27:1085:90459:16:17:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(Porter 2011). Dismissed filers may also lose their health insurance or change family environments
27:1086:90557:17:16:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in a way that impacts health. Unfortunately, it is not possible to link information on morbidity,
27:1087:90654:16:17:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:health insurance, or family status to our data. The precise mechanisms for our estimated mortality
27:1088:90752:17:0:72:456:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:effect therefore remain unclear, and likely include a combination of these factors.
28:1089:90837:0:23:257:355:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:E. External Validity
28:1090:90857:23:17:72:540:685:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In this section, we discuss the external validity of our results for Chapter 13 filers in our estimation
28:1091:90961:17:16:72:382:668:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:sample, Chapter 13 filers in our full sample, and Chapter 7 filers.
28:1092:91028:16:17:88:539:652:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:One potential caveat of our results is that we estimate the effects of Chapter 13 protection for
28:1093:91124:17:16:72:540:635:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the marginal recipient of bankruptcy protection. Recall that our instrumental variable identification
28:1094:91225:16:17:72:540:619:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:strategy identifies the impact of Chapter 13 for filers whose bankruptcy decision is altered by judge
28:1095:91326:17:16:72:540:602:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:assignment due to disagreement on whether or not they should receive bankruptcy protection. This
28:1096:91422:16:17:72:540:586:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:local average treatment effect may or may not reflect the average treatment effect of bankruptcy for
28:1097:91522:17:16:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:all filers. To investigate heterogeneous treatment effects across unobservable debtor characteristics,
28:1098:91624:16:16:72:540:553:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we estimate MTEs (Heckman and Vytlacil 2005). In our setting, the MTE estimates illustrate how
28:1099:91718:16:17:72:540:537:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the outcomes for debtors on the margin of bankruptcy protection change as we move from more
28:1100:91809:17:16:72:540:520:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:strict to more lenient judges. Thus, the MTE estimates shed light on the types of filers who benefit
28:1101:91909:16:17:72:540:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:most from bankruptcy protection, and whether our local average treatment effects are likely to
28:1102:92003:17:16:72:299:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:apply to filers who are further from the margin.
28:1103:92051:16:17:88:539:471:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:To calculate the MTE function, we follow Doyle (2007) and predict the probability of bankruptcy
28:1104:92146:17:16:72:540:454:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection using a probit model with judge leniencyZijctas the only explanatory variable. We then
28:1105:92243:16:16:72:540:438:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:predict the relationship between each outcome and the predicted probability of receiving bankruptcy
28:1106:92342:16:17:72:540:422:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection using a local quadratic estimator with a bandwidth of 0.069.16The first derivative of this
28:1107:92443:17:16:72:540:405:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:relationship is then evaluated at each percentile of the predicted probability of receiving bankruptcy
28:1108:92545:16:17:72:540:389:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:protection using the coefficients from the local quadratic regression. We calculate standard errors
28:1109:92644:17:16:72:540:372:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:using the standard deviation of MTE estimates from a bootstrap procedure with 250 iterations
28:1110:92736:16:17:72:342:356:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:adjusted for clustering at the office by filing month level.
28:1111:92796:17:16:88:539:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Appendix Figure 11 reports the MTE of Chapter 13 protection for earnings, employment, five-
28:1112:92887:16:16:72:540:323:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:year mortality, and five-year home foreclosure. The MTE function for earnings is increasing in the
28:1113:92985:16:17:72:540:307:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:predicted probability of bankruptcy protection, while the MTE function for mortality and home
28:1114:93078:17:16:72:540:290:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:foreclosure are decreasing in the predicted probability of bankruptcy protection. The upward slope
28:1115:93176:16:17:72:540:274:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the earnings MTE and downward slope in the mortality and home foreclosure MTEs suggest that
28:1116:93270:17:16:72:540:257:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers on the margin of bankruptcy who are assigned to the most lenient judges experience the largest
28:1117:93371:16:17:72:540:241:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:gains when granted bankruptcy protection. These are likely filers with unobservable characteristics
28:1118:93470:17:16:72:540:224:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that make them the least likely to be granted bankruptcy in the first place, as the margin for
28:1119:93564:16:17:72:540:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:relatively lenient judges should entail relatively less deserving filers.  This interpretation of the
28:1120:93665:17:16:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimates suggests that the impact of Chapter 13 on earnings is modestly larger for less deserving
28:1121:93763:16:16:72:540:175:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:debtors. Conversely, the MTE function for employment is flat, suggesting that the employment
28:1122:93855:16:18:72:413:159:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f4:effects do not differ systematically across unobservable characteristics.17
28:1123:93930:18:15:83:539:141:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:16Following Doyle (2007), the pilot bandwidth was chosen by minimizing the sum of squared errors between the
28:1124:94038:15:11:72:540:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:local quadratic estimator and a fourth-degree polynomial model for each outcome. Larger bandwidths lead to more
28:1125:94149:11:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:linear relationships and flatter MTE estimates. We chose the minimum bandwidth across all outcomes to explore
28:1126:94258:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:variations from linearity. The local quadratic estimator was chosen as it is thought to have better properties when
28:1127:94373:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:evaluating first derivatives (Fan and Gijbels 1996). Results are nearly identical for higher and lower polynomials and
28:1128:94491:11:7:72:219:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:both larger and smaller bandwidths.
28:1129:94526:7:0:83:539:75:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:17Appendix Figure 12 reports the MTE of Chapter 13 protection for 401k contributions, DI, and SSI, and Appendix
29:1130:94639:0:17:88:539:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A second potential caveat is we are only able to use instrumental variables design in bankruptcy
29:1131:94735:17:16:72:540:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:offices that randomly assign filings to judges. Recall from Table 1 that our estimation sample is
29:1132:94832:16:17:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:broadly similar to the full sample of Chapter 13 filings. Yet, it is possible that the two groups of
29:1133:94932:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers differ in some unobservable way. We provide estimates of the impact of Chapter 13 protection
29:1134:95031:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in our full sample using an event study methodology that compares the outcomes of granted and
29:1135:95124:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:dismissed filers. Our event strategy design is in the spirit of Bound’s (1989) analysis of accepted
29:1136:95223:16:17:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and rejected DI applicants, and more recent work estimating the effects of job loss on subsequent
29:1137:95320:17:16:72:540:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:outcomes (Jacobson, Lalonde, and Sullivan 1993, von Wachter, Song, and Manchester 2009, Sullivan
29:1138:95416:16:16:72:185:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and von Wachter 2009).
29:1139:95438:16:17:88:539:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Intuitively, our event study design uses granted filers as a treatment group and dismissed filers
29:1140:95535:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:as a control group. The key identifying assumption is that dismissed filers would have experienced
29:1141:95633:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the same outcomes as granted filers had they been granted bankruptcy protection. However, recall
29:1142:95729:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:from Figure 3 that dismissed filers start with lower earnings and experience larger earnings shocks
29:1143:95828:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:before filing than granted filers. To account for the difference in pre-filing earnings between granted
29:1144:95931:17:16:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and dismissed filers, we include individual fixed effects that control for time-invariant differences
29:1145:96032:16:16:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:across filers. To account for different earnings trends, we also include fixed effects for the decile of
29:1146:96136:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:predicted propensity score separate by event time. We estimate the propensity score using an OLS
29:1147:96232:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:regression of an indicator for bankruptcy protection on gender, race, five-year age bins, five-years
29:1148:96332:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of baseline employment, five-years of baseline earnings, and office by month fixed effects. We then
29:1149:96431:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:group filers into deciles of the predicted probability of receiving bankruptcy protection. Thus, our
29:1150:96531:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:event strategy design compares the outcomes of granted and dismissed filers with similar predicted
29:1151:96629:17:16:72:324:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:probabilities of being granted bankruptcy protection.
29:1152:96682:16:36:88:407:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Formally, we estimate various specifications of the following model:
29:1153:96750:36:0:163:234:311:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f10:yit=αi+αt+
29:1154:96760:0:27:246:256:324:8:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f12:5∑
29:1155:96762:27:0:237:259:297:8:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f16:k=−5
29:1156:96766:0:0:261:322:311:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f10:βkPscoreki+
29:1157:96777:0:27:334:344:324:8:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f12:5∑
29:1158:96779:27:0:325:346:297:8:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f16:k=−5
29:1159:96783:0:37:349:539:311:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:γkBankruptcyki+εit(12)
29:1160:96805:37:17:71:539:274:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereyitis our outcome of interest,αiare individual fixed effects that control for time-invariant
29:1161:96902:17:16:71:539:257:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:differences across filers,αtare year fixed effects that control for time-varying factors that affect all
29:1162:97006:16:17:71:539:241:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:filers similarly, andPscorekiis the decile of predicted propensity score separate by event timek.
29:1163:97103:17:16:72:539:224:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:Bankruptcykiis an indicator for being in thek-th period before or after filing interacted with having
29:1164:97204:16:17:72:540:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:been granted bankruptcy protection. The coefficientsγktherefore measure the evolution ofyitfor
29:1165:97298:17:16:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:granted bankruptcy filers relative to dismissed filers. We omit effects for the year prior to filing, so
29:1166:97402:16:16:72:540:175:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that all parameter estimates measure differences relative to this base year. For mortality and home
29:1167:97501:16:33:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:foreclosure where we do not observe differences in the year prior to filing, we omit the year of filing.
29:1168:97605:33:11:72:540:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Figure 13 reports the MTE of the job mobility outcomes described in Table 7. Consistent with our main results, the
29:1169:97719:11:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:MTE functions for DI and SSI are decreasing in the predicted probability of bankruptcy protection and the MTE
29:1170:97828:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:functions for same state, same industry, same job, and average firm wage are increasing in the predicted probability
29:1171:97944:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:of bankruptcy protection. These results suggest that filers on the margin of bankruptcy who are assigned to the most
29:1172:98060:11:11:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:lenient judges experience the largest gains in stability when granted bankruptcy protection. The MTE functions for
29:1173:98174:11:0:72:300:71:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:401k contributions, same county, and job tenure are flat.
30:1174:98233:0:17:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:As a result, our event study estimates for these outcomes are likely attenuated towards zero as we
30:1175:98331:17:16:72:502:692:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:attribute any treatment effects in the year of filing to the effects of bankruptcy protection.
30:1176:98425:16:17:88:539:676:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Appendix Figure 14 presents event study estimates of equation (12) for Chapter 13 filers in our
30:1177:98520:17:16:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimation sample and all Chapter 13 filers in our data. The “full” sample is restricted to a ten
30:1178:98617:16:17:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:percent random draw of first-time filers for the non-foreclosure results for computational reasons.
30:1179:98716:17:16:72:540:626:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The home foreclosure sample includes all first-time filers in counties covered by DataQuick. Standard
30:1180:98817:16:17:72:274:610:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:errors are clustered at the individual level.
30:1181:98862:17:16:88:539:593:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There is a large and statistically significant effect of Chapter 13 protection on all of our outcomes
30:1182:98963:16:16:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in both the estimation sample and the full sample of Chapter 13 filers. Over the first five post-filing
30:1183:99066:16:17:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:years, filers receiving Chapter 13 protection earn $4,034 to $5,581 more than dismissed filers in
30:1184:99163:17:16:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:our estimation sample, and $3,783 to $5,114 more in our full sample. Employment is 2.6 to 8.1
30:1185:99256:16:17:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:percentage points higher in our estimation sample, and 2.3 to 6.7 percentage points higher in our
30:1186:99353:17:16:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:full sample. Five-year mortality and foreclosure are 2.0 and 10.9 percentage points lower in our
30:1187:99449:16:17:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimation sample, and 1.5 and 12.9 percentage points lower in our full sample. Thus, the impact
30:1188:99545:17:16:72:462:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Chapter 13 protection appears to be similar in our full and estimation samples.
30:1189:99627:16:16:88:539:462:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A final concern is that our analysis has focused on Chapter 13 bankruptcy, which makes up about
30:1190:99722:16:17:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:25 percent of all bankruptcy filings. Recall that there is not enough variation in the treatment of
30:1191:99821:17:16:72:540:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Chapter 7 cases to estimate the effects of Chapter 7 protection using our instrumental variables
30:1192:99917:16:17:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:strategy.  Appendix Figure 14 presents results for Chapter 7 protection using our event study
30:1193:100010:17:16:72:540:396:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:methodology described above. We again restrict the non-foreclosure results to a ten percent random
30:1194:100108:16:17:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:draw of all first-time filers. The home foreclosure sample includes all first-time filers in counties
30:1195:100209:17:16:72:180:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:covered by DataQuick.
30:1196:100230:16:16:88:539:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The effect of Chapter 7 protection is much more modest than the effect of Chapter 13 protection.
30:1197:100326:16:17:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Over the first five post-filing years, filers granted Chapter 7 bankruptcy protection earn $1,639 to
30:1198:100426:17:16:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:$1,936 more than dismissed filers, and are 2.4 to 2.8 percentage points more likely to be employed.
30:1199:100525:16:17:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Filers granted Chapter 7 protection are 1.7 percentage points less likely to experience a home
30:1200:100619:17:16:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:foreclosure after five years, but are no more or less likely to be deceased. The more modest impact
30:1201:100718:16:17:72:540:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Chapter 7 is somewhat surprising given the fact that, in principle, all Chapter 7 filers have the
30:1202:100818:17:16:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:option of filing under Chapter 13. The more modest benefits of Chapter 7 therefore seem likely to
30:1203:100915:16:17:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:be the result of the different composition of filers under each Chapter. There may also be important
30:1204:101015:17:16:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:impacts of Chapter 7 on other ex-post outcomes that we are not measuring here, such as credit
30:1205:101108:16:16:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:availability or cost, that compare more favorably with respect to Chapter 13. Finally, it is possible
30:1206:101209:16:17:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that our event study design is less plausible for Chapter 7 cases. Less than two percent of Chapter
