30:1207:101308:17:16:72:540:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:7 cases are dismissed, with these cases typically dismissed due to fraud or an inability to complete
30:1208:101408:16:17:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the bankruptcy paperwork correctly. Thus, dismissed Chapter 7 filers may not be a suitable control
30:1209:101506:17:0:72:184:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:group for granted filers.
31:1210:101533:0:28:261:351:708:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:VI. Conclusion
31:1211:101547:28:16:72:540:680:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In this paper, we estimate the impact of Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection on subsequent labor
31:1212:101640:16:16:72:540:664:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:supply, mortality, and home foreclosure. We find that Chapter 13 increases the marginal recipient’s
31:1213:101739:16:17:72:540:648:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:annual earnings in the first five post-filing years by $5,562, a 25.1 percent increase from the baseline
31:1214:101843:17:16:72:540:631:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mean. Employment increases by 6.8 percentage points over the same time period, an 8.3 percent
31:1215:101936:16:17:72:540:615:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:increase from the baseline mean. Five-year mortality is 1.2 percentage points lower, a 30.0 percent
31:1216:102035:17:16:72:540:598:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:decrease from the dismissed filer mortality rate, with five-year foreclosure rates falling by 19.1
31:1217:102133:16:17:72:540:582:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:percentage points, a more than one hundred percent decrease from the dismissed filer foreclosure
31:1218:102229:17:16:72:540:565:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:rate. We find evidence consistent with the results being driven by increased incentive to work and
31:1219:102327:16:16:72:540:549:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:increased economic stability following the receipt of bankruptcy protection. A descriptive analysis of
31:1220:102429:16:17:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:granted and dismissed filers further suggests the impacts are driven by the deterioration of outcomes
31:1221:102530:17:16:72:378:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:among dismissed filers as opposed to any gains by granted filers.
31:1222:102595:16:17:88:539:500:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our results provide new evidence on the ex-post benefits of debt relief. These results are par-
31:1223:102690:17:16:72:540:483:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ticularly important in light of the on-going debate surrounding the use of debt relief and mortgage
31:1224:102789:16:17:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:modification to stimulate the economy. Work by Mulligan (2008), Hall (2011), and Eggertsson and
31:1225:102884:17:16:72:540:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Krugman (2012) suggests that household borrowing constraints can help explain the severity of the
31:1226:102981:16:17:72:540:434:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:recession, while Mian and Sufi (2012) show that regional differences in debt overhang can explain
31:1227:103078:17:16:72:540:417:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:differences in unemployment. Our estimates also suggest that the restrictions on bankruptcy fil-
31:1228:103174:16:16:72:540:401:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ing introduced by the 2005 Bankruptcy Abuse Prevention and Consumer Protection Act may have
31:1229:103265:16:17:72:280:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:important adverse consequences on debtors.
31:1230:103307:17:16:88:539:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The main limitation of our analysis is that we are not able to estimate the impact of bankruptcy
31:1231:103403:16:17:72:540:352:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:laws on ex-ante borrowing costs or behavior.  There may also be important ex-post impacts of
31:1232:103495:17:16:72:540:335:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:bankruptcy protection on outcomes such as credit availability that we are unable to measure with
31:1233:103591:16:17:72:540:319:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:our data. Finally, our analysis has focused on Chapter 13 bankruptcy, which makes up about 25
31:1234:103684:17:16:72:540:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:percent of all bankruptcy filings. This paper should therefore be viewed as a first step towards
31:1235:103780:16:0:72:420:286:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:characterizing the impact of consumer bankruptcy protection on debtors.

36:1388:114752:11:11:77:545:435:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:all first-time Chapter 13 filers between 1992 and 2005 in the 42 offices that randomly assign filings to judges. Judge
36:1389:114870:11:11:77:545:424:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:leniency is the leave-one-out mean rate of granting Chapter 13 bankruptcy protection for the assigned judge minus
36:1390:114983:11:11:77:545:413:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:the leave-one-out mean rate of granting bankruptcy protection for the court in the same filing year. To construct the
36:1391:115100:11:11:77:545:402:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:binned scatter plot, we first regress an indicator for discharge on office by month-of-filing fixed effects and calculate

36:1393:115337:11:11:77:545:380:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:to aid in the interpretation of the plot. The solid line shows the best linear fit estimated on the underlying micro data
36:1394:115458:11:11:77:545:369:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:estimated using OLS. The coefficients show the estimated slope of the best-fit line including office by month-of-filing

57:1834:145552:20:11:77:545:281:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Notes: These figures plot marginal treatment effects and associated 95 percent confidence intervals.  The sample
57:1835:145664:11:11:77:545:270:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:includes first-time filings between 1992 and 2005 in the 42 offices that randomly assign cases to judges. The foreclosure
57:1836:145785:11:11:77:545:259:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:sample includes the subset of those filings originating in county by year bins with foreclosure data coverage. We
57:1837:145898:11:11:77:545:248:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:predict the probability of bankruptcy protection using our leave-one-out measure of judge leniency. We then predict
57:1838:146013:11:11:77:545:237:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:the relationship between each outcome and the predicted probability of receiving bankruptcy protection using a local
57:1839:146129:11:11:77:545:226:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:quadratic estimator with bandwidth 0.069. The estimates of the first derivative of this relationship are then evaluated
57:1840:146248:11:11:77:545:215:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:at each percentile of the predicted probability. Standard errors are calculated using a bootstrap procedure with 250
57:1841:146364:11:11:77:545:204:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:iterations. All monetary values are expressed in real 2000 dollars divided by 1,000. Earnings information comes
57:1842:146475:11:11:77:545:193:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:from the W-2, and is averaged over the first five post-filing years. Employment is an indicator for non-zero wage
57:1843:146588:11:11:77:545:182:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:earnings on the W-2, and is averaged over the first five post-filing years. Five-year mortality is an indicator for being
57:1844:146709:11:11:77:545:171:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:deceased within the first five post-filing years using information from the Death Master File. Five-year foreclosure is
57:1845:146828:11:10:77:545:160:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:an indicator for a filer’s home receiving a notice of default, receiving a notice of transfer or sale, or being transferred
57:1846:146951:10:0:77:496:150:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:to a REO or a guarantor within the first five post-filing years using real estate records from DataQuick.

62:1909:151133:0:11:77:545:710:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:Notes: These figures plot event study results of the impact of Chapter 13 and Chapter 7 bankruptcy protection.
62:1910:151243:11:11:77:545:699:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:The Judge IV sample includes all first-time filings between 1992 and 2005 in the 42 offices that randomly assign
62:1911:151355:11:11:77:545:688:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:cases to judges.  The full sample includes a 10 percent random sample of all first-time filings between 1992 and
62:1912:151467:11:11:77:545:677:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:2005 in the 72 bankruptcy courts that allow electronic access to their dockets. The foreclosure sample includes all
62:1913:151582:11:11:77:545:666:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:filings originating in county by year bins with foreclosure data coverage. We report the coefficient on an indicator for
62:1914:151702:11:11:77:545:655:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:receiving bankruptcy protection interacted with the specified year. We control for individual, year, and propensity
62:1915:151817:11:11:77:545:644:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:score decile by year fixed effects. The propensity score is using a probit regression of an indicator for discharge on
62:1916:151935:11:11:77:545:633:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:gender, race, five-year age bins, five years of baseline employment entered individually, five years of baseline earnings
62:1917:152056:11:11:77:545:622:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:entered individually, office fixed effects, and filing year fixed effects. We then split the sample into deciles and interact
62:1918:152181:11:11:77:545:611:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:each decile with year indicators for the five years before and after filing, omitting the year prior to filing. Standard
62:1919:152301:11:11:77:545:600:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:errors are clustered at the individual level. Year 0 indicates the year a debtor files for bankruptcy protection. All
62:1920:152418:11:10:77:545:589:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:monetary values are expressed in real 2000 dollars. Earnings information comes from the W-2. Employment is an
62:1921:152527:10:11:77:545:579:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:indicator for non-zero wage earnings on the W-2. Mortality is an indicator for being deceased in the indicated year
62:1922:152642:11:11:77:545:568:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:using information from the Death Master File. Foreclosure is an indicator for a filer’s home receiving a notice of
62:1923:152756:11:11:77:545:557:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:default, receiving a notice of transfer or sale, or being transferred to a REO or a guarantor. See text for additional
62:1924:152874:11:0:77:106:546:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:details.
